- **content**:
  - **title**: Tarkasangraha
  - **sections**:
    - **Item 1**:
      - **title**: Tarkasangraha
      - **number**: `1`
      - **verses**:
        - **Item 1**:
          - **verse_number**: `1`
          - **original_text**: Opening Prayer:<br>निधाय हृदि विश्वेशं विधाय गुरुवन्दनम् ।<br>बालानां सुखबोधाय क्रियते तर्कसंग्रहः ॥ १ ॥
          - **commentaries**:
            - **Item 1**:
              - **author**: English Paraphrase
              - **commentary**: 1. Devotedly meditating on the Lord of the universein my heart, and offering my salutations to the preceptor,<br>I proceed to compile the book (known as) theTarkasamgraha for the easy comprehension of the beginners.<br>[1. Following the usual orthodox practice, the author begins his<br>work with a mangalācarana (or an invocatory verse), consisting of<br>a prayer to his Chosen Deity, and a salutation to the preceptor.<br>The second line of the verse incidentally also deals with the four<br>incentives as is the practice before a literary treatise is commenced.<br>Mangalācaraņa at the commencement of a work is an auspicious<br>act, consisting of invocatory verses to the deity adored by the Author.<br>The prayer is a supplication to the deity to help in the unhindered<br>completion of the work. The four incentives (anubandha catuştaya)<br>are: (a) adhikārin, a competent student; (b) visaya, the subject matter;<br>(c) sambandha, relation; and (d) prayojana, aim or purpose. A study<br>of any subject will appeal only to one who has an intense desire<br>(ārthitva) for knowing the subject matter. He should also have the<br>capacity to understand (śaktatva) to fully profit from the study. Here,<br>the student competent to enter upon the study is a 'beginner' according<br>to the Author. Bāla means a beginner who has both arthitva and<br>śaktatva and who is free from aparyudasțatva, ie free from disabilities<br>and possesses the opportunity. (Comp: Sri Sankara's com. on Tait.up.<br>II-1) The subject matter is the elements of Nyaya-Vaiśeşika. The<br>relation is of the treated and the treatise, ie of the subject matter<br>and the explainer treatise. The purpose is easy comprehension of the<br>subject matter, a knowledge of which will eventually lead one to<br>the highest goal of human life. Prayojana is the last link in the<br>chain of incentives. Unless a promise is held out no one will seek<br>knowledge. It is said:<br>prayojanamanuddiśya na mando'pi pravartate- without desiring profit<br>not even a dullard takes any initiative.']
            - **Item 2**:
              - **author**: Sanskrit Commentary
              - **commentary**: विश्वेश्वरं साम्बमूर्ति प्रणिपत्य गिरां गुरुम् ।<br>टीकां शिशुहितां कुर्वे तर्कसंग्रहदीपिकाम् ॥<br>चिकीर्षितस्य ग्रन्थस्य निर्विघ्नपरिसमाप्त्यर्थं शिष्टाचारानुमितश्रुतिबोधितकर्तव्यताक-<br>इष्टदेवतानमस्कारात्मकं मङ्गलं शिष्यशिक्षायै ग्रन्थतो निबध्नंश्चिकीर्षितं प्रतिजानीते ।<br>निधायेति । ननु मङ्गलस्य समाप्तिसाधनत्वं नास्ति । मङ्गले कृतेऽपि किरणावल्यादौ<br>समाप्त्यदर्शनात्, मङ्गलाभावेऽपि कादम्बर्यादौ समाप्तिदर्शनाच्च अन्वयव्यतिरेकाभ्यां<br>व्यभिचारादिति चेत् न । किरणावल्यादौ विघ्नबाहुल्यात्समाप्त्यभावः । कादम्बर्यादौ<br>ग्रन्थाद्बहिरेव मङ्गलं कृतमतो न व्यभिचारः । ननु मङ्गलस्य (ग्रन्थादौ) कर्तव्यत्वे<br>किं प्रमाणमिति चेत् न । शिष्टाचारानुमितश्रुतेरेव प्रमाणत्वात् । तथा हि मङ्गलं<br>वेद-बोधितकर्तव्यताकमलौकिकाविगीतशिष्टाचारविषयत्वाद्दर्शादिवत् ।. भोजनादौ व्यभिचार<br>वारणाय अलौकिकेति । रात्रिश्राद्धादौ व्यभिचारवारणाय अविगीतेति । शिष्टपदं स्पष्टार्थम् ।<br>न कुर्यान्निष्फलं कर्म इति जलताडनादेरपि निषिद्धत्वात् । तर्व्यन्ते प्रतिपाद्यन्ते इति<br>तर्काः द्रव्यादिपदार्थास्तेषां संग्रहः सङ्क्षेपेण स्वरूपकथनं क्रियत इत्यर्थः । कस्मै<br>प्रयोजनायेत्यत आह । सुखबोधायेति । सुखेनानायासेन यो बोधः पदार्थज्ञानं तस्मा<br>इत्यर्थः । ननु बहुषु तर्कग्रन्थेषु सत्सु किमर्थमपूर्वोऽयं ग्रन्थः क्रियत इत्यत आह ।<br>बालानामिति । तेषामतिविस्तृतत्वाद्वालानां बोधो न जायत इत्यर्थः । ग्रहणधारणपटुर्बालः<br>न तु स्तनन्धयः । किं कृत्वा क्रियत इत्यत आह । निधायेति । विश्वेशं<br>जगन्नियन्तारम् । हृदि निधाय नितरां स्थापयित्वा सदा तद्धयानपरो भूत्वेत्यर्थः ।<br>गुरूणां विद्यागुरूणां, वन्दनं नमस्कार, विधाय कृत्वेत्यर्थः ।।
            - **Item 3**:
              - **author**: English Translation
              - **commentary**: Dīpikā:<br>Prostrating before the Lord of the Universe, who is one<br>with the Divine Mother and is the master of words. I begin<br>the commentary called Tarkasangraha Dīpika, which will benefit<br>beginners. To achieve the unhindered completion of the treatise<br>that is desired to be undertaken, and also as an instruction<br>to the students, the author pays his devout homage to his<br>Chosen Deity with an appropriate Propitiatory Verse (Mangala<br>śloka) at the very commencement of the treatise. This<br>time-honoured practice is enjoined by the Vedic Text as is<br>inferred from the authority derived from the observances of<br>good people.<br>[2. Sistācāra-anumita: Siştah is one who performs an act enjoined<br>in the Veda in conformity with his knowledge of the Tattvas based<br>on the Veda- Vedokta tattvaĵnānena veda vihita Karmakarī - Nilakantha.]<br>Objection: Now, a propitiatory verse does not possess the<br>efficacy to accomplish unhindered completion (of the treatise);<br>because, it is seen that books like Kādambarī etc., are incomplete<br>though they were undertaken with appropriate propitiatory<br>verses, while works like Kiraņāvalī etc., were completed without<br>any hindrance even though no propitiatory verses were<br>incorporated at the beginning. Thus, there is deviation in<br>the law of 'positive and negative factors.'<br>[3. The efficacy of Mangala in the completion of a work is questioned<br>here by citing the deviation in the law of anvaya and Vyatireka<br>ie in the presence and absence of its causes. Two entities are said<br>to be related to each other when they are attended with anvaya<br>and Vyatireka. Anvaya is the method of agreement or the positive<br>factor and the Vyatireka is the method of disagreement or the negative<br>factor. The presence of cause but the absence of the effect is the<br>anvaya Vyabhicara. In the above instance, Marigalacarana is the cause;<br>samāpti or completion of the work is the effect. The example cited<br>to highlight the anvaya Vyabhicāra is the book Kadambarī, the celebrated<br>story of the heroine Kādambarī by Bāņa. The book was commenced<br>with a mangalācarana, but was not completed during the author's<br>life-time. So, here, there is deviation in the law of correlation as<br>the effect does not exist though the cause exists. Similarly, in Kiraņāvalī,<br>though mangalācarana was not performed, completion was achieved<br>by the author. Here there is the absence of the cause while the<br>effect is present, thus violating the law of negative factor. This deviation<br>in the law of both the positive and negative factors renders the<br>argument that a propitiatory verse before commencing any treatise<br>possesses the efficacy to accomplish its unhindered completion,<br>inaffective. Therefore, it is objected that the mangalacarana at the<br>commencement of a work has nothing to do with its completion.]<br>Reply: It is not so; because the non-completion is due<br>to the abundance of obstacles in works like Kādambarī etc.<br>(i.e., the propitiatory verse was not capable of overcoming<br>the obstacles since the latter overwhelmed the former). In<br>books like Kiraṇāvalī etc., the propitiatory prayer was done<br>by the author extraneously (i.e., mentally or in his previous<br>birth) without incorporating the same in the book. Therefore,<br>there is no deviation.<br>[4. The purpose of mangala śloka is to remove obstacles. Completion<br>of the work will result if the obstacles are removed.]<br>Question: But what is the authority for the necessity to<br>incorporate the invocatory verse (at the beginning of a treatise)?<br>Answer: Vedic injunction inferred from the observation of<br>good practices of virtuous men is verily the authority. Propitiation<br>is known to have been enjoined in the Vedic Text because<br>it is (a) a topic that cannot be known from sources other<br>than the Vedas (alaukika), (b) is uncensured (avigīta in the<br>Dharma Śāstras), and (c) is the object of the observances<br>by virtuous men, like the Darśa etc. In order to aviod deviation<br>in (daily practices like) eating etc propitiatory prayer is said<br>to be alaukika (because eating etc are also the objects of<br>observances by virtuous men and are uncensured. To guard<br>against this deviation, alaukika is inserted). The term avigīta<br>is inserted to remove overapplication in obsequial rites etc.<br>performed during night. The word śista (good man) is used<br>only for clarity (and is not superfluous) because it is said:<br>'One should not engage oneself in fruitless labour,' as even<br>striking water without any purpose is prohibited in the scriptures.<br>Exposition or elucidation is Tarka. The meaning is: It<br>is a compendious elucidation of the nature of the seven<br>ontological categories beginning with substance. What is the<br>purpose? The answer is: sukha bodhāya, for the easy<br>comprehension, ie by studying which an easy comprehension<br>of the knowledge of the categories is obtained.<br>Question: For what purpose is this new work undertaken<br>when there are already many tarka granthas in existence?<br>Answer: Bālānām - for beginners; the meaning is that the<br>beginners are unable to grasp the elucidation of the nature<br>of categories since in those books (already in existence) it<br>is treated in great detail. Beginner is one who is dexterous<br>in grasping and retaining in memory (the elucidation of the<br>nature of categories etc), and not one who is merely a suckling<br>(but has studied grammar, poetry etc).<br>Question: By doing what is this (work) composed?<br>Answer: Nidhāya, devoutly meditating in the heart the Lord<br>who is of the nature of Auspiciousness and who is the Controller<br>of the Universe, and offering salutations to the teachers of<br>knowledge (this treatise is composed).
        - **Item 2**:
          - **verse_number**: `2`
          - **original_text**: 2. Classification of the categories (which are the Reals):<br>द्रव्यगुणकर्मसामान्यविशेषसमवायाऽभावाः सप्तपदार्थाः ॥ २ ॥
          - **commentaries**:
            - **Item 1**:
              - **author**: English Paraphrase
              - **commentary**: 2. Substance, quality, action, generality, particularity,<br>inherence, and negation are the seven categories.
            - **Item 2**:
              - **author**: Sanskrit Commentary
              - **commentary**: पदार्थान् विभजते । द्रव्येति । पदस्यार्थः पदार्थः इति व्युत्पत्त्याभिधेयत्वं<br>पदार्थसामान्यलक्षणम् (लभ्यते) । ननु विभागादेव सप्तत्वे सिद्धे सप्त (पद) ग्रहणं<br>व्यर्थमिति चेत्, न अधिकसंख्याव्यवच्छेदार्थकत्वात् । नन्वतिरिक्तः पदार्थः प्रमितो<br>वा न वा । नाऽद्यः प्रमितस्य निषेधायोगात् । न द्वितीयः प्रतियोगिप्रमितिं विना<br>निषेधानुपपत्तेरिति चेत्, न । पदार्थत्वं द्रव्यादिसप्तान्यतमत्वव्याप्यमिति व्यवच्छेदार्थकत्वात्<br>(सप्तग्रहणम्) । ननु सप्तान्यतमत्वं सप्तभिन्नभिन्नत्वमिति वक्तव्यम् । सप्तभिन्नस्याप्रसिद्धया<br>कथं सप्तान्यतमत्वव्याप्तिनिश्चय इति चेत्, न । द्रव्यादिसप्तान्यतमत्वं नाम<br>द्रव्यादिभेदसप्तकाभाववत्त्वम् । अतो दोषविरहात् । एवमग्रेऽपि द्रष्टव्यम् ॥
            - **Item 3**:
              - **author**: English Translation
              - **commentary**: Dīpikā:<br>Categories are being enumerated. Category is a thing<br>corresponding to a name. In the light of this derivation, the<br>general definition of categories is an object named or denoted<br>by the corresponding word.<br>Objection: Since by classification itself we get seven<br>categories, the use of the word sapta is superfluous.<br>Reply: Not so; because, the insertion of the word sapta<br>is used to exclude a larger number.<br>Objection: Is then, the additional category (ie the eighth<br>category sought to be precluded) a known entity or is it<br>unknown? It cannot be the former, for, a known object cannot<br>be held as having no existence at all; it cannot be the latter<br>too; for, how can an unknown object be repudiated when<br>the knowledge of its counter-entity has not become the content<br>of one's mind at all?<br>[5. ie the non-existence of an object can be experienced only<br>when that object which is the pratiyogin or the counter-reality<br>of non-existence is recollected. If recollected, it cannot be repudiated.<br>If not, the negation of the eighth category too cannot be proved.]<br>Reply: It is not so; because, by padārthatva (ie the fact<br>of being a category) is meant the fact of categoriness being<br>pervasive of any one of the seven categories beginning with<br>substance. Thus, the term sapta serves the purpose of exclusion<br>(of a larger number).<br>[6. Annambhatta here provides a positive interpretation to the<br>preclusive term seven. He interprets the term to mean that the mention<br>of the categories as seven only indicates the fact of a category being<br>pervasive - vyāpya in the sense of its being one among the seven<br>categories. That is to say, when it is said, X is the vyāpya of<br>Y, it means where there is X, there is also Y. So, wherever there<br>is the fact of being a padartha, there is also the fact of its being<br>one among the seven categories. To put it simply, to be a padārtha<br>is to be any of the seven categories beginning with dravya, ie it<br>may be dravya or guna or karma etc. When thus interpreted in<br>a positive way, the defects that would arise in a negative interpretation<br>as pointed out by the opponents, would not occur.]<br>Objection: If it is so, any-one-ness (in each of the seven<br>categories) must be admitted to mean differenceness from what<br>is other than the seven. But since a thing other than the<br>seven is unknown, how can the pervasion of any-one-ness<br>be determined (ie only if there exists an eighth padārtha<br>it would be possible for it to be other than all those seven.<br>When the eighth padārtha itself is unknown, there cannot<br>be the one which is different from seven)?<br>Reply: It is not so; because, any-one-ness in each of the<br>seven categories beginning with substance means the<br>non-existence of difference of seven categories beginning with<br>substance in any one category. As such there is no defect<br>in the above statement. Further, it has to be interpreted similarly<br>whenever occasions arise.<br>[7. The idea is this: Each one of the seven categories is different<br>from every category other than itself. Thus the quality of being different<br>from each one of the seven categories is known to exist in all<br>the other six categories. But the aggregate of the negations of all<br>the seven categories is not known to exist in any particular category.<br>Will it not be known to exist in the eighth if there existed one<br>such? Thus, the usage of the word sapta serves to exclude the<br>existence of the eighth category. Again, if the aggregate of the negations<br>of all the seven categories is not known anywhere, it will lead to<br>the admittance that the seven categories do not exist at all, because<br>without the knowledge of sapta, bheda cannot be negated as without<br>the knowledge of counter-entity, a thing cannot be negated; for instance,<br>a pot cannot be negated without the knowledge of the counter-entity<br>of negation, viz, pot. If saptabheda were to be admitted as not<br>existing anywhere in a particular place, then its counter-entity sapta<br>too will have to be admitted as having no existence; if the negation<br>of pot is not admitted, the pot also should not be admitted as<br>having existence. The reply to this objection is as follows: As each<br>of the seven bhedas is known to exist severally in all other six<br>categories it can be argued that each of the seven categories and<br>its negation are well-known. As such, by the very argument that<br>the aggregate of negations of the seven does not exist in one particular<br>place, we are forced to admit that saptabheda has its existence<br>everywhere, viz, in all the seven categories.]
        - **Item 3**:
          - **verse_number**: `3`
          - **original_text**: 3. Classification of substance:<br>तत्र द्रव्याणि पृथिव्यप्तेजोवाय्वाकाशकालदिगात्ममनांसि<br>नवैव ॥ ३ ॥
          - **commentaries**:
            - **Item 1**:
              - **author**: English Paraphrase
              - **commentary**: 3. Of the seven categories, the substances are only nine, viz, earth, water, light, air, ether, time, space, soul and mind.
            - **Item 2**:
              - **author**: Sanskrit Commentary
              - **commentary**: द्रव्यं (द्रव्याणि) विभजते । तत्रेति । तत्र द्रव्यादिमध्ये । द्रव्याणि नवैवेत्यन्वयः ।<br>कानि तानि इत्यत आह । पृथिवीति । ननु तमसो दशमद्रव्यस्य विद्यमानत्वात्कथं<br>नवैव द्रव्याणीति । तथा हि । नीलं तमश्चलतीत्यबाधितप्रतीतिबलान्नीलरूपाधारतया<br>क्रियाधारतया च तमसो द्रव्यत्वं तावत् सिद्धम् । तत्र तमसो नाकाशादिपञ्चकेऽन्तर्भावः<br>रूपवत्त्वात् । अत एव न वायौ, स्पर्शाभावात् सदागतिमत्त्वाभावाच्च । नापि तेजसि,<br>भास्वररूपाभावात् उष्णस्पर्शाभावाच्च । नापि जले, शीतस्पर्शाभावात् नीलरूपवत्त्वाच्च ।<br>नापि पृथिव्यां, गन्धाभावात् स्पर्शरहितत्वाच्च । तस्मात्तमो दशमद्रव्यमिति चेत्, न ।<br>तमसस्तेजोऽभावरूपत्वात् । तथा हि । तमो न रूपिद्रव्यमालोकासहकृतचक्षुर्ग्राह्यत्वा-<br>दालोकाभाववत् । रूपिद्रव्यचाक्षुषप्रमायामालोकस्य कारणत्वात् । तस्मात्<br>प्रौढप्रकाशकतेजस्सामान्याभावस्तमः, तत्र नीलं तमश्चलति इति प्रत्ययो भ्रमः । अतो<br>नव द्रव्याणीति सिद्धम् । द्रव्यत्वजातिमत्त्वं गुणवत्त्वं वा द्रव्यसामान्यलक्षणम् ।<br>लक्ष्यैकदेशावृत्तित्वमव्याप्तिः । यथा गोः कपिलत्वम् । अलक्ष्ये लक्षणस्य वर्तनमतिव्याप्तिः ।<br>यथा गोः श्रृङ्गित्वम् । लक्ष्यमात्रावृत्तित्वमसंभवः । यथा गोरेकशफवत्त्वम् ।<br>एतद्दूषणत्रयरहितधर्मो लक्षणम् । स एवासाधारणधर्म इत्युच्यते ।<br>लक्ष्यतावच्छेदकसमनियतत्वमसाधारणत्वम् । व्यावर्तकस्यैव लक्षणत्वे व्यावृत्तावभिधेयत्वादौ<br>चातिव्याप्तिरतस्तद्वारणाय तद्भिन्नत्वं धर्मविशेषणं देयम् । व्यवहारस्यापि लक्षणप्रयोजनत्वे<br>तन्न देयम् । व्यावृत्तेरपि व्यवहारसाधनत्वात् । ननु गुणवत्त्वं न द्रव्यलक्षणम्,<br>आद्यक्षणावच्छिन्नघटे उत्पन्नविनष्टघटे चाव्याप्तेरिति चेत्, न ।<br>गुणसमानाधिकरणसत्ताभिन्नजातिमत्त्वस्य विवक्षितत्वात् । नन्वेवमपि एकं रूपं रसात्पृथक्<br>इति व्यवहाराद्र्पादावतिव्याप्तिरिति चेत्, न । एकार्थसमवायादेव तादृशव्यवहारोपपत्तौ<br>गुणे गुणानङ्गीकारात् ।
            - **Item 3**:
              - **author**: English Translation
              - **commentary**: Dīpikā:<br>Substance is being divided by the Text: tatra. ....Among<br>the seven categories, substances are only nine. What are they?<br>The answer is given in the Text: Earth.... etc.<br>Objection: How can substances be enumerated as only nine<br>when a tenth substance, darkness (Tamas) exists? The substance<br>darkness is proved since it is the substratum of colour and<br>movement that arises from the irrefutable knowledge, blue<br>darkness moves. Moreover, darkness cannot be included in<br>any one of the five substances beginning with ether because<br>of the absence of rupa in them; not in air, because of<br>the absence of touch and of constant motion in darkness;<br>nor does darkness get included in light because of the absence<br>of brilliant colour and hot-touch; nor in water as it is devoid<br>of cold-touch and as it is also the substratum of blue colour;<br>nor in earth, owing to the absence of odour and as it is<br>devoid of touch. Therefore, darkness is the tenth substance.<br>Reply: Not so; because, darkness is of the nature of the<br>negation of light. Nor can darkness be a substance having<br>colour for the simple reason that the presence of light is<br>an essential factor in perceiving a substance having colour,<br>whereas darkness is perceived only when there is no light.<br>Darkness is, therefore, nothing but the general absence of<br>intense and powerful luminous light. Here the cognition: blue<br>darkness moves is erroneous knowledge. Thus it is proved<br>that substances are only nine <br>[8. The above objection is raised by the Mīmāmsakas who consider<br>Tamas darkness to be a distinct substance and prove its existence<br>by the argument that Tamas possesses rūpa colour and motion.<br>None can deny that darkness is bluish or black. Also, it is seen<br>to move in the sky, thus possessing motion; moreover, it cannot<br>be said to belong to any of the group mentioned above by the<br>Vaiśeşikas. Thus, Mīmāmsakas say that darkness must be accepted<br>as the tenth substance.<br>Annambhatta upholds the Vaiśeşika position by asserting that Tamas<br>or darkness is not any positive entity at all; it is nothing but the<br>absence of light. If darkness had colour, as the Mīmāmsakas say,<br>it then ought to be seen in light; the uniform condition to apprehend<br>colour or form is the presence of light. Whereas, darkness melts<br>away or disappears in the presence of light. Sometimes, an object<br>is not revealed in insufficient light; it is because of the insufficiency<br>of the power of light to reveal an object and not because of the<br>presence of darkness, for, darkness and light never co-exist. Then<br>how to explain the fact of darkness being experienced by all? Annambhatta<br>explains such experiences as illusory. Nīlakantha, however, says that<br>keeping in view the law of parsimony, it would be simpler to consider<br>darkness as the absence of bright light rather than consider it as<br>the tenth substance. See also Siddhanta Muktāvalī of Viśvanātha]<br>The general definition of substance is something possessing<br>the genus substanceness (dravyatva), or possessing a quality.<br>Partial inapplication (avyāpti) is non-application of the definition<br>to some of the things defined, eg the brownness of a cow. [9. This definition is too narrow a definition as there are also<br>cows of other colours]<br>Overapplicability (ativyāpti) is the application of the definition<br>to things not intended to be defined, eg the horn of a cow.[10. Because, the definition of the cow as an animal having a<br>horn includes buffaloes also since they too have horns, but are not<br>cows.]<br>A definition which is wholly inapplicable to any of the things<br>defined is total inapplicability (asambhava), eg the uncloven<br>hoof of a cow.[11. Because the hoof of a cow is never uncloven.] So, that attribute alone can be a definition<br>which is free from these three types of defects, eg the definition<br>of a cow as an animal having dewlap. This is called the<br>special characteristic mark of a cow. 'Special characterness'<br>(Asādhāraṇatva) consists in being reciprocally co-extensive with<br>the adjunct that delimits the scope of things sought to be<br>defined (ie it is a characteristic mark that covers all things<br>denoted by the definition). To explain: wherever there is cowness<br>which is the delimiting adjunct of the cow, there is also<br>dewlap and where there is no cowness there is also no<br>dewlap. This is reciprocal co-existence (samaniyatatva).[12. Asādhāraṇatva is lakṣyatā-avacchedaka-samaniyatatvam. That<br>which is intended to be defined is laksya or the definitum. When<br>we want to define a cow, cow becomes the laksya. Thus, anything<br>can become a laksya. Every lakşya has in it laksyatā, ie the quality<br>of being a laksya. Thus, when a cow is a laksya, it has in it<br>the laksyatā also. Though lakṣyatā exists in all laksyas, lakṣyatā and<br>cowness together exist only in a cow; similarly, lakṣyatā and horseness<br>together exist only in a horse. Thus, it is the generic attribute cowness that restricts the laksyata from extending itself to a horse or to<br>any other laksya. Similarly, horseness restricts laksyata from extending<br>itself to any other laksya. Thus, cowness or horseness are avacchedakas<br>or adjuncts to laksyata, which set limit to the extensive pervasion<br>of laksyata. Therefore, laksyata-avacchedaka means an adjunct to<br>laksyata.<br>Sama-niyatatvam: When two things are invariably co-existent to<br>each other, they are sama-niyata; eg where there is dewlap there<br>will be cowness and where there is cowness there will be dewlap.<br>Here, dewlap is samaniyata to cowness and vice versa. It is admitted<br>that laksana as such will be vyāvartaka, ie that which renders the<br>lakşya distinguished from all the rest. As such, the laksana of laksana,<br>viz laksyata-avacchedaka-samaniyatatvam would apply to all laksanas<br>that are vyāvartakas in this instance dewlap which is vyāvartaka,<br>since it distinguishes the cow from the rest. As such,<br>laksyata-avacchedaka-samaniyatatvam rightly applies to dewlap thus:<br>Where there is laksyata-avacchhedaka (cowness) there is dewlap and<br>where there is dewlap there is also cowness. But this laksana of<br>laksyata-avacchedaka-samaniyatatvam extends to vyāvṛtti (itarabheda)<br>which is other than laksya. Vyāvṛtti ie the quality of being different<br>from everything other than itself, is itarabheda, while vyāvartaka is<br>that which occasions the inference of the birth of itarabheda. But<br>the laksana of laksana (ie asādhāraṇatvam) happens to extend to<br>gavetarabheda (ie the quality of being distinct from all other than<br>the cow) inasmuch as both cowness and gavetarabheda are co-existent<br>to each other thus: Where there is cowness, there is gavetarabheda<br>and where there is gavetarabheda there is cowness. Further, this laksana<br>extends to abhidheyatva too, which is not vyāvartaka. Abhidheyatva<br>is all-pervasive. There is no category which is not abhidheya. As<br>such a category other than abhidheya cannot exist. When abhidheyatvam<br>is accepted as laksana of a padartha, padārtha becomes laksya,<br>padārthatvam becomes the laksyata-avacchedaka. In abhidheyatvam, the<br>definition of definition viz laksyata-avacchedaka-samaniyatatvam happens<br>thus: Wherever, there is padarthatvam, there is abhidheyatvam, and<br>wherever there is abhidheyatvam there is padārthatvam.]<br>Objection: Since the function of definition is the exclusion<br>of the thing defined from everything other than itself, this<br>definition of definition (asādhāranatva) suffers from the defect<br>of overapplicability in vyāvṛtti and abhidheyatva.<br>Reply: To avoid this overapplicability in itarabheda and<br>abhidheyatva, the attribute, other than itarabheda and abhidheyatva<br>must be added to asādhāranatva. If it is said that vyāvahārika<br>laksana (ie the definition that is the cause of conventional<br>usage of words) is also the definitum to asādhāranatva, then,<br>we need not add (the attribute of tadbhinnatvam) because,<br>vyāvṛtti is the cause of conventional expression of words like<br>cow etc.<br>Objection: The general definition of substance cannot be<br>as that possessing quality, since it suffers from the defect<br>of partial applicability in a jar in the first moment of its<br>creation and destruction. [13. According to Vaisesika ontology, an effect-substance, ie any<br>created thing, is without any guna or quality at the first instant<br>of its production or emergence, and that it is only after that first<br>instant that a product may come to acquire a quality. So, according<br>to his own tenets, a substance is without any quality at the moment<br>of its emergence. How can then he define a substance as that having<br>the property of quality? Or, the definition should be modified to<br>avoid this defect; otherwise, it would amount to saying that a substance<br>at the moment of its emergence is different from itself at its subsequent<br>moments.]<br>Reply: Not so; because of the desirability of amplifying<br>the definition as that which possesses the generic attribute<br>(which is less comprehensive) different from existence<br>(sattābhinna, sattā being more comprehensive) and which<br>co-exists at the same time with quality in the same substratum. [14. This amplification of the definition of substance is not vulnerable<br>to the charge of avyapti. The jati of dravya, viz, dravyatva or<br>substanceness is present in every dravya. Also, satta, the universal<br>existence also is there in a substance. To avoid the defect of<br>overapplicability in satta, it is said sattābhinna. A dravya at the<br>moment of its emergence and/or destruction may not have in it<br>any guna but it does have dravyatva<br>the universal substanceness.<br>This substance is also present in every substance where a guna<br>is present. So, it is guna samānādhikaraņa. This avoids the defect<br>of ativyapti.]<br>Objection: Even then, in conventional usages like, one colour,<br>different from taste, etc there is overapplicability in colour<br>etc.<br>Reply: Not so; because, such conventional usages are current<br>only because of ekārthasamavāya; and also because the statement<br>quality exists in quality is unacceptable. [15. The idea is this: the characteristic of substance is defined<br>guņasamānādhikaraņasattābhinnajātimatvam to avoid the defect of<br>ativyāpti in quality as also in action. The opponent points out that<br>by the above definition the defect of ativyāpti cannot be avoided,<br>and in order to establish this, he provides two examples: (a) The<br>conventional expression one colour is well known. Here, in colour,<br>colourness or qualityness inheres and also its adjunct one exists. One<br>comes under number (sarikhyā) which is one of the 24 qualities.<br>Thus colourness becomes the common substratum of sankhyā guna<br>which is different from satta. Thus, in colour, there is sattābhinnajāti<br>which is also the gunasamānādhikaraņa. Further, this laksana of dravya<br>is found in rupa also. (b) In the example, rūpam rasāt prthak, rūpa<br>has prthaktva as its qualifying adjunct which is also one of the 24<br>qualities. Rūpatva jāti inheres in rupa and prthaktva also is in rupa.<br>So, rūpatva becomes the samānādhikarana of prihaktva guna. Thus,<br>in rupa, there is sattābhinnajāti while being also the<br>guna-samānādhikarana. This is refuted as follows: Guna inheres only<br>in dravya. Of course, there are conventional expressions like one<br>colour etc. The intended relationship here is samavāya, ie inherent<br>relationship. As this relation is not between the substratum colour<br>and the oneness, there will be no overapplicability in colour.]
        - **Item 4**:
          - **verse_number**: `4`
          - **original_text**: 4. Classification of Quality:<br>रूप-रस-गन्ध-स्पर्श-संख्या-परिमाण-पृथक्त्व-संयोग-विभाग-<br>परत्वा-ऽपरत्व-गुरुत्व-द्रवत्व-स्नेह-शब्द-बुद्धि-सुख-दुःखेच्छा<br>द्वेष-प्रयत्न-धर्माधर्म-संस्काराः चतुर्विंशतिर्गुणाः ॥ ४ ॥
          - **commentaries**:
            - **Item 1**:
              - **author**: English Paraphrase
              - **commentary**: 4. Colour, taste, odour, touch, number, magnitude,<br>separateness, conjunction, disjunction, remoteness,<br>proximity, weight, fluidity, viscidity, sound, intellect,<br>pleasure, pain, desire, aversion, volition, merit, demerit<br>and tendency are the twenty-four qualities.
            - **Item 2**:
              - **author**: Sanskrit Commentary
              - **commentary**: गुणान्विभजते । रूपेति । द्रव्यकर्मभिन्नत्वे सति सामान्यवान् गुणः । गुणत्वजातिमान्वा ।<br>ननु लघुत्वकठिनत्वमृदुत्यादीनां विद्यमानत्वात् कथं चतुर्विंशतिर्गुणा इति चेत्, न ।<br>लधुत्वस्य गुरुत्वाभावरूपत्वान्मृदुत्वकठिनत्वयोः अवयवसंयोगविशेषत्वात् ।
            - **Item 3**:
              - **author**: English Translation
              - **commentary**: Dīpikā:<br>Qualities are sub-divided by the statement in the Text:<br>rūpa...... Quality is that which possesses generality while at<br>the same time being quite different from substance and actions; [16. According to the Vaiśeşika doctrine, jāti inheres only in dravya<br>(Substance), guna (Quality) and karma (Action). If it is said merely<br>that quality is that which possesses sāmānya (generality), then, there<br>would occur ativyāpti in dravya and guna as they too are samanyas.<br>To avoid this, the definition is qualified by the statement while being<br>different from dravya and karma. If guna is defined merely as something<br>other than dravya and karma, then ativyapti will occur in samānya,<br>viśeṣa, samavāya and abhāva. To avoid this defect it is qualified<br>by samānyavān as sāmānya inheres only in dravya, guna and karma.]<br>or, it is that which possesses the generic attribute, qualityness. [17. Naturally, a doubt may arise as to why the second definition<br>is given while the first definition itself is free of defects, and, hence<br>should be sufficient. Nīlakantha suggests that though the first definition<br>is logically sound, the second one seems to be better by virtue<br>of its brevity and simplicity (lāghavatā). Also, the first definition is<br>based on bheda (difference) and samānya (generality) while the second<br>one is based on samanya only.]<br>Objection: Since the existence of qualities like levity, softness,<br>hardness etc is known, how can the qualities be enumerated<br>as twenty-four only?<br>Reply: They are not included because lightness is of the<br>nature of the absence of heaviness, while softness and hardness<br>are simply various degrees of density of contact among the<br>parts.
        - **Item 5**:
          - **verse_number**: `5`
          - **original_text**: 5. Classification of Action (Karma-Vibhāga):<br>उत्क्षेपणापक्षेपणाकुञ्चनप्रसारणगमनानि पञ्च कर्माणि ॥ ५ ॥
          - **commentaries**:
            - **Item 1**:
              - **author**: English Paraphrase
              - **commentary**: 5. Action is of five kinds; they are: upward motion,<br>downward motion, contraction, expansion and motion<br>from one place to another.
            - **Item 2**:
              - **author**: Sanskrit Commentary
              - **commentary**: कर्म विभजते । उत्क्षेपणेति । संयोगभिन्नत्वे सति संयोगासमवायिकारणं कर्म<br>कर्मत्वजातिमद्वा । भ्रमणादीनामपि गमने अन्तर्भावान्न पञ्चत्वविरोधः ।।
            - **Item 3**:
              - **author**: English Translation
              - **commentary**: Dīpikā:<br>Action is being sub-divided by the Text: utksepana.....<br>Action is the non-inherent cause of conjunction while being<br>quite different from conjunction (ie action itself is not<br>conjunction); or, it is that which possesses the genus of Action<br>(Karmatvajātimān). [18. As in the earlier verse, here also, Annambhatta provides<br>alternate definition for Karma. The first definition has two conditions;<br>(a) samyogabhinnatva; (b) samyogasamavāyi kāraṇa. The first condition<br>prevents the defect of ativyapti in sariyoga inasmuch as the Vaiśeşikas<br>hold that conjunction can be due to karma or due to conjunction.<br>So, if Karma is merely defined as the asamavāyi kāraṇa of Samyoga,<br>then, the definition would also extend to instances where conjunctions<br>are due to conjunctions. This ativyāpti is avoided by the first condition.<br>Again, if the second term is not inserted, then, the definition would<br>apply to substance as well inasmuch as substance which is not karma<br>is also a condition of conjunction (though samavāyi - inherent). Thus,<br>the insertion of asamavāyi keeps out substance from the definition,<br>and obviates the defect of Ativyāpti in substance]<br>Objection: Since other kinds of actions like gyration exist,<br>the enumeration of action as five is inappropriate.<br>Reply: Not so; since actions like gyration etc are also included<br>under motion, there is no contradiction with the enumeration<br>of action as five. [19. Actions like bhramaņa (rotation), recanā (purging or breathing<br>out), syandana (flowing) etc are not considered by Annambhatta as<br>distinct forms of karma; rather, they are only various varieties of<br>gamana. Hence, the charge of incomplete enumeration is not sustainable]
        - **Item 6**:
          - **verse_number**: `6`
          - **original_text**: 6. Classification of Generality:<br>परमपरं चेति द्विविधं सामान्यम् ॥ ६ ॥
          - **commentaries**:
            - **Item 1**:
              - **author**: English Paraphrase
              - **commentary**: 6. Generality is of two kinds; the more<br>comprehensive, and the less comprehensive.
            - **Item 2**:
              - **author**: Sanskrit Commentary
              - **commentary**: सामान्यं विभजते । परमिति । परमधिकदेशवृत्ति । अपरं न्यूनदेशवृत्ति ।<br>सामान्यादिचतुष्टये जातिर्नास्ति ॥
            - **Item 3**:
              - **author**: English Translation
              - **commentary**: Dīpikā:<br>Generality is being sub-divided by the Text: param.....<br>That which pervades more space is the more comprehensive,<br>and that which pervades less space is the less comprehensive.<br>There is no generality in the four categories beginning with<br>generality. [20. Sāmānya is the general feature found in many entities. This<br>has been explained more elaborately later - under section IX-17.<br>Sāmānya as satta resides in all dravyas, gunas and karmas. Of the<br>Samanya, the Sattā sāmānya is the widest; sāmānyas like jāti reside<br>only in their respective entities, eg dravyata in dravya, gotva in go<br>etc. It is in this sense that sattā-sāmānya is said to be the widest.<br>According to Vaiśeşika theory, this Samanya resides only in the first<br>three of the seven padārthas.]
        - **Item 7**:
          - **verse_number**: `7`
          - **original_text**: 7. Particularities:<br>नित्यद्रव्यवृत्तयो विशेषास्त्वनन्ता एव ॥ ७ ॥
          - **commentaries**:
            - **Item 1**:
              - **author**: English Paraphrase
              - **commentary**: 7. But, particularities abiding in eternal substances<br>are innumerable indeed.
            - **Item 2**:
              - **author**: Sanskrit Commentary
              - **commentary**: विशेषं विभजते । नित्येति । पृथिव्यादिचतुष्टयपरमाणवः आकाशादिपञ्चकं च<br>नित्यद्रव्याणि ।
            - **Item 3**:
              - **author**: English Translation
              - **commentary**: Dīpikā:<br>Particularities are being divided by the Text: nitya.... The<br>atoms of four substances beginning with earth (prthivī) and<br>the five substances beginning with ether (ākāśa) are the eternal<br>substances (in which particularities inhere).[21. Viśeṣās are the differentiating features subsisting in eternal<br>substances and they are infinite inasmuch as the eternal substances<br>in which they inhere, are infinite.]
        - **Item 8**:
          - **verse_number**: `8`
          - **original_text**: 8. Inherence:<br>समवायस्त्वेक एव ॥ ८ ॥
          - **commentaries**:
            - **Item 1**:
              - **author**: English Paraphrase
              - **commentary**: 8. But inherence is only one.
            - **Item 2**:
              - **author**: Sanskrit Commentary
              - **commentary**: समवायस्य भेदो नास्तीत्याह । समवायस्त्विति ।
            - **Item 3**:
              - **author**: English Translation
              - **commentary**: Dīpikā:<br>By the Text: Inherence..., it is said that there is no difference<br>in inherence. [22. According to Vaiśeşika Theory, Samavāya is a unitary entity<br>and as such does not admit of any division. (For definition of Samavāya,<br>see section IX-18)]
        - **Item 9**:
          - **verse_number**: `9`
          - **original_text**: 9. Classification of Negation:<br>अभावश्चतुर्विधः - प्रागभावः, प्रध्वंसाभावः, अत्यन्ताभावः,<br>अन्योन्याभावश्चेति ॥ ९ ॥
          - **commentaries**:
            - **Item 1**:
              - **author**: English Paraphrase
              - **commentary**: 9. Negation is fourfold: antecedent negation;<br>destructive negation; absolute negation and mutual<br>negation.
            - **Item 2**:
              - **author**: Sanskrit Commentary
              - **commentary**: अभावं विभजते । प्रागभावेति ।
            - **Item 3**:
              - **author**: English Translation
              - **commentary**: Dīpikā:<br>Negation is being sub-divided in the Text: abhāva.....[23. Antecedent negation is the non-existence of a thing before<br>its production, eg the expression, the cloth will come into existence,<br>when the cloth is about to be produced. The expression, this jar<br>is destroyed is an example of destructive negation. Thus, the existence<br>of a thing is confined to the intermediary period of antecedent negation<br>and destructive negation. Absolute negation is non-existence of a thing<br>at ail times - past, present, and future, as when we say: On this<br>spot there is no jar. Mutual negation is mutual dissimilarity, like the<br>expression, a jar is not a cloth. The existence of a jar in a cloth,<br>or of a cloth in a jar, is denied as there is the total absence<br>of any semblance between jar and cloth.<br>Here ends the Section I where Annambhatta deals with the<br>enumeration (uddeśa) of the sapta padārthas and their further sub-divisions<br>as recognised by the Vaiśeşika School of Thought. Section II deals<br>mostly with lakşaņā (definition) and parīksā (critical examination) of<br>the categories.]
        - **Item 10**:
          - **verse_number**: `10`
          - **original_text**: CHARACTERISTICS OF SUBSTANCES<br>1. Earth:<br>तत्र गन्धवती पृथिवी । सा द्विविधा नित्याऽनित्या च । नित्या<br>परमाणुरूपा । अनित्या कार्यरूपा । पुनस्त्रिविधा शरीरेन्द्रिय<br>विषयभेदात् । शरीरमस्मदादीनाम् । इन्द्रियं गन्धग्राहकं घ्राणम् ।<br>तच्च नासाग्रवर्ति । विषयो मृत्पाषाणादिः ॥ १ ॥
          - **commentaries**:
            - **Item 1**:
              - **author**: English Paraphrase
              - **commentary**: 1. Of the substances, earth is that which has odour<br>(as its inherent) quality. It is of two varieties; eternal<br>and non-eternal. Eternal is the atomic and non-eternal<br>is the product. Again, it is threefold: body, organ, and<br>object. Body is that like ours; that which grasps odour<br>is the olfactory organ and it abides at the tip of the<br>nose. The earthy objects are like clay, stone and such<br>other things.
            - **Item 2**:
              - **author**: Sanskrit Commentary
              - **commentary**: तत्रोद्देशक्रमानुसारात् प्रथमं पृथिव्या लक्षणमाह । तत्रेति । नाम्ना पदार्थसंकीर्तनमुद्देशः ।<br>उद्देशक्रमे च सर्वत्रेच्छैवं नियामिका । ननु सुरभ्यसुरभ्यवयवाख्धे द्रव्ये परस्परविरोधेन<br>गन्धानुत्पादादव्याप्तिः । न च तत्र गन्धप्रतीत्यनुपपत्तिरिति वाच्यम् । अवयवगन्धस्यैव<br>तत्र प्रतीतिसंभवेन चित्रगन्धानङ्गीकारात् किं चोत्पन्नविनष्टघटादावव्याप्तिरिति चेत् न ।<br>गन्धसमानाधिकरणद्रव्यत्वापरजातिमत्त्वस्य विवक्षितत्वात् । ननु जलादावपि गन्धप्रतीतिरिति<br>चेत् न । अन्वयव्यतिरेकाभ्यां पृथिवीगन्धस्यैव तत्र भानाङ्गीकारात् । ननु कालस्य<br>सर्वाधारतया सर्वेषां लक्षणानां कालेऽतिव्याप्तिरिति चेत् न । सर्वाधारताप्रयोजकभिन्नसंबन्धेन<br>लक्षणत्वस्य विवक्षितत्वात् । पृथिवीं विभजते । सा द्विविधेति । नित्यत्वं<br>ध्वंसाप्रतियोगित्वम् । अनित्यत्वं ध्वंसप्रतियोगित्वम् । प्रकारान्तरेण विभजते । पुनरिति ।<br>आत्मनो भोगायतनं शरीरम् । यदवच्छिन्नात्मनि भोगो जायते तद्भोगायतनम् ।<br>सुखदुःखसाक्षात्कारो भोगः । शब्देतरोद्भूतविशेषगुणानाश्रयत्वे सति ज्ञानकारणमनः<br>संयोगाश्रयत्वमिन्द्रियत्वम् । शरीरेन्द्रियभिन्नो विषयः । एवं च गन्धवच्छरीरं पार्थिवशरीरम्,<br>गन्धवदिन्द्रियं पार्थिवेन्द्रियम्, गन्धवान् विषयः पार्थिवविषय इति तत्तलक्षणं बोध्यम् ।<br>पार्थिवशरीरं दर्शयति । शरीरमिति । इन्द्रियं दर्शयति । इन्द्रियमिति । गन्धग्राहकमिति<br>प्रयोजनम् । घ्राणमिति संज्ञा । नासाग्रेत्याश्रयोक्तिः । एवमुत्तरत्र ज्ञेयम् । पार्थिवविषयं<br>दर्शयति । मृत्पाषाणादीति ।
            - **Item 3**:
              - **author**: English Translation
              - **commentary**: Dīpikā:<br>Following the Nyaya order of exposition, the characteristic<br>mark of earth is defined next to enumeration of categories<br>etc. Uddeśa is enumeration of categories by naming them.<br>One's intent alone is the regulator in the sequence of<br>enumeration. [24. That is to say, there is no hard and fast rule regarding<br>the sequence of enumeration; it may start from any category]<br>Objection: Now, in a substance composed of parts having<br>fragrant and foul smell, there is the non-birth of odour owing<br>to the two kinds of odour being mutually incompatible. So,<br>here is the defect of partial applicability of the definition.[25. The opponent points out the defect of avyapti if the definition<br>of earth were to be taken for granted. In support of his objection,<br>he puts forward the argument mentioned in the Dipika. If the thing<br>then becomes odourless, what would be the nature of the product?<br>Since both the component parts are earth, the product too would<br>be only earth, but without smell as the two smells cancel each<br>other. Here, thus, is an instance of earth without any smell. Then,<br>how can the definition of earth as having smell for its characteristic<br>be sustained, as the definition suffers from the defect of avyāpti<br>as pointed out above? This is the idea]<br>Nor can it be said that, in that case, apprehension of odour<br>in the substance is rendered impossible, because the smell<br>experienced in the component parts will certainly be apprehended<br>in the substance also. Further, variegated odour is unacceptable<br>to the Siddhantin. [26. The argument that there is variegated odour (citra gandha)<br>in the substance consequent on the odour apprehended in the substance<br>being the odour existing in the component parts, is unacceptable.]Also, there is partial applicability (of the<br>definition in the earthy products like) jar etc. just created<br>and destroyed.[27. According to the Naiyāyikas, a product in the first moment<br>of its creation and destruction, is supposed to be without any attribute.]<br>Reply: Not so; (ie there is no defect of partial applicability<br>in products just produced and destroyed); because, of the<br>desirability of amplifying the definition as that which possesses<br>a generic attribute less comprehensive than substanceness while<br>co-existing with odour in the same substratum.<br>Objection: In water also odour is apprehended. So, here<br>is overapplicability (because even water etc besides earth possess<br>odour).<br>Reply: Not so; because, the apprehension of odour in water<br>is due to the contact of minute particles of earth mixed<br>with it and this can be proved by applying the method of<br>affirmation and negation. [28. Where there is water mixed up with earth substance there<br>is odour and where there is the absence of such mix-up there is<br>also the absence of odour this is the method of affirmation and<br>negation] Odour appears to be present in<br>water owing to the relation of samyukta samavāya (ie inherence<br>in a thing which has come into contact with another thing).<br>Objection: All the definitions suffer from the defect of<br>over-applicability in Time since Time is the container of<br>everything (because everything exists in Time).<br>Reply: No such defect occurs since each definition has<br>to be defined by its relation to substance other than its<br>relation to Time (and Space) which are the essential factors,<br>since they are the supports of everything.<br>Earth is being divided by the Text: sa dvividhā.... Eternality<br>is being non-liable to destruction. Non-eternality is being liable<br>to destruction. Earth is further classified by the Text: punah....<br>Body is the seat of the soul for experiences (of the fruits<br>of actions, good, bad, and mixed). That (ie the body) which<br>delimits the soul in which enjoyments take place, is the seat<br>of enjoyment. Enjoyment is the immediate experience of pleasure<br>and pain. Organ is being the substratum of contact with<br>mind which causes knowledge, while not being the substratum<br>of any manifested special quality except sound. Object is that<br>which is different from body and organ. Thus, a body having<br>smell, is the earthy body, an organ producing the knowledge<br>of odour is the earthy organ, and an object possessing odour<br>is the earthy object. The respective characteristic marks (of<br>body, organ, and object) are thus to be understood. Earthy<br>body is shown by the Text: śarīram.... The earthy organ is<br>indicated by the Text: indriyam.... Gandhagrāhakam in the<br>Text indicates the necessity of the organ to apprehend odour.<br>Ghrānam in the Text indicates the name of the organ.<br>Nāsāgravarti in the Text indicates the seat of the organ. These<br>terms are to be understood in similar ways hereafter too<br>(whenever they occur). Visaya in the Text indicates earthy<br>objects like clay and stone.
        - **Item 11**:
          - **verse_number**: `11`
          - **original_text**: 2. Water: (ap)<br>शीतस्पर्शवत्यः आपः । ता द्विविधाः नित्या अनित्याश्च ।<br>नित्याः परमाणुरूपाः । अनित्याः कार्यरूपाः । पुनः त्रिविधाः<br>शरीरेन्द्रियविषयभेदात् । शरीरं वरुणलोके । इन्द्रियं रसग्राहकं<br>रसनं जिह्वाग्रवर्ति । विषयः सरित् समुद्रादिः ॥ २ ॥
          - **commentaries**:
            - **Item 1**:
              - **author**: English Paraphrase
              - **commentary**: 2. Water is that which has cold touch. It is of<br>two kinds: eternals and non-eternals; eternals are of<br>the nature of atoms and non-eternals are of the nature<br>of products; it is again of three varieties: body, organ,<br>and object. Its body is in the region of Varuna; organ<br>is the gustatory sense by which one perceives savour,<br>and it is located at the tip of the tongue. Objects<br>are rivers, oceans and the like.
            - **Item 2**:
              - **author**: Sanskrit Commentary
              - **commentary**: अपां लक्षणमाह । शीतेति । उत्पन्नविनष्टजलेऽव्याप्तिवारणाय शीतस्पर्शसमाना-<br>धिकरणद्रव्यत्वापरजातिमत्त्वं विवक्षितम् । "शीतं शिलातलम्" इत्यादौ जलसंबन्धादेव<br>शीतस्पर्शभानमिति नातिव्याप्तिः । अन्यत्सर्वं पूर्वरीत्या व्याख्येयम् ॥
            - **Item 3**:
              - **author**: English Translation
              - **commentary**: Dīpikā:<br>The Text gives the characteristic mark of water: Sīta....<br>To remove partial applicability in water just produced and<br>destroyed, the definition of water should be interpreted as<br>having the generic attribute which is less comprehensive than<br>substanceness, and which has the same substratum with cold<br>touch. [29. The defect of avyapti in water that is just produced and<br>destroyed is avoided by expanding the definition as water endowed<br>with its universal jāti (generic attribute) which is co-existent with cold<br>touch. Jalatva (which is the jati of water) is always co-located with<br>cold touch, that is to say, both cold-touch and jalatva have the<br>same substratum. Water which perishes immediately after it comes<br>into existence has in it its jāti Jalatva which admittedly co-exists<br>with cold touch. Thus, there is no defect of avyapti] Further, there is no overapplicability in slabs of stones<br>where coldness is felt because, the feeling of cold touch<br>in them is owing to the presence of water in the stone. [30. Again, this definition suffers from the defect of ativyāpti<br>inasmuch as the cold surface of a piece of stone, for example,<br>is cold to the touch but it is not water; else, that piece of stone<br>should be considered as a watery substance which is absurd. Thus,<br>the definition extends to objects not intended for. Here, the explanation<br>is the same offered to explain the presence of smell in water mixed<br>with earthen particles. Here also, the cold feel of the stone is due<br>to its contact with water.]<br>Everything else has to be interpreted as before.
        - **Item 12**:
          - **verse_number**: `12`
          - **original_text**: 3. Light: (Tejas)<br>उष्णस्पर्शवत् तेजः । तच्च द्विविधं, नित्यमनित्यं च । नित्यं<br>परमाणुरूपम् । अनित्यं कार्यरूपम् । पुनः त्रिविधं<br>शरीरेन्द्रियविषयभेदात् । शरीरं आदित्यलोके प्रसिद्धम् । इन्द्रियं<br>रूपग्राहकं चक्षुः कृष्णताराग्रवर्ति । विषयः चतुर्विधः,<br>भौम-दिव्य-औदर्य-आकरज भेदात् । भौमं वह्नयादिकम् ।<br>अबिन्धनं दिव्यं विद्युदादि । भुक्तस्य परिणामहेतुरौदर्यम् । आकरजं<br>सुवर्णादि ॥ ३ ॥
          - **commentaries**:
            - **Item 1**:
              - **author**: English Paraphrase
              - **commentary**: 3. Light is that which has hot touch. And, that is of two kinds: eternal and non-eternal. Eternal is of the nature of atom and the non-eternal is of the nature of the product. It is again of three kinds: body, organ and object. The body is well known in the solar region. The organ is the (visual scene) eye which perceives colour and it has for its seat the forepart of the dark pupil of the eye. The object is of four kinds: earthy, heavenly, gastric and mineral. The earthy variety is the common fire and the like; lightning produced from watery fuel is the heavenly variety; the gastric variety is that which causes digestion of food eaten; lustrous metals like gold etc belong to the mineral variety.
            - **Item 2**:
              - **author**: Sanskrit Commentary
              - **commentary**: तेजसो लक्षणमाह । उष्णस्पर्शवदिति । 'उष्णं जलम्' इति प्रतीतेस्तेजः संयोगानुविधायित्वान्नातिव्याप्तिः । विषयं विभजते । भौमेति । ननु 'सुवर्ण पार्थिवं' पीतत्वाद्गुरुत्वात् हरिद्रावत् इति चेत् न । अत्यन्तानलसंयोगे सति घृतादौ द्रवत्वनाशदर्शनन, जलमध्यस्थघृतादौ तन्नाशादर्शनेन च असति प्रतिबन्धके पार्थिवद्रवत्वनाशाग्निसंयोगयोः कार्यकारणभावावधारणात्सुवर्णस्य अत्यन्तानलसंयोगे सत्यनुच्छिद्यमानद्रवत्वाधिकरणत्वेन पार्थिवत्वाऽनुपपत्तेः पीतद्रव्यद्रवत्वनाशप्रतिबन्धकतया द्रवद्रव्यान्तरसिद्धौ नैमित्तिकद्रवत्वाधिकरणतया जलत्वानुपपत्तेः रूपवत्तया वाय्वादिष्वनन्तर्भावात्तेजसत्वसिद्धिः । तस्योष्णस्पर्शभास्वररूपयोरुपष्टम्भक पार्थिवरूपस्पर्शाभ्यां प्रतिबन्धादनुपलब्धिः । तस्मात् सुवर्णं तैजसमिति सिद्धम् ।
            - **Item 3**:
              - **author**: English Translation
              - **commentary**: Dīpikā:<br>The characteristic mark of light is given in the Text:<br>Usna.... There is no defect of overapplicability in the knowledge:<br>This water is hot; because, such knowledge arises in water<br>owing to the contact of fire with water. Object is classified<br>by the Text: Bhauma....<br>Objection: Gold is an earthy product, because, it possesses<br>yellowish colour and is heavy like turmeric etc.<br>Reply: Not so; because, on the observation of the fact<br>that fluidity in earthy substances like clarified butter vanish<br>when extreme heat is applied; while the fluidity of clarified<br>butter placed in the midst of water does not vanish even<br>when subjected to extreme heat (as long as there is water),<br>we arrive at an understanding of an effect-cause relation between<br>the destruction of fluidity in an earthy substance and contact<br>with fire in the absence of any counter-acting agent. When<br>extreme heat is applied to gold, the fluidity of melted gold<br>is not destroyed even in the absence of a counteracting agent.<br>Therefore, gold is not an earthy substance. This is proved<br>by the presence of a distinct fluid substance in the yellow<br>metal possessing the capacity to obstruct the destruction of<br>fluidity (even when heat is applied). Nor can it be water<br>since fluidity in gold is only occasional (whereas water has<br>its fluidity as its natural quality); nor can gold be included<br>in air etc since gold possesses colour. Gold is, therefore,<br>light. Here, the feeling of heat and bright colour (natural<br>to light) are not apprehended due to the obstruction caused<br>by the colour and touch of the supportive earthy particles.<br>Thus is proved that gold is light (belonging to mineral variety).
        - **Item 13**:
          - **verse_number**: `13`
          - **original_text**: 4. Air (Vāyu)<br>रूपरहितः स्पर्शवान् वायुः । स द्विविधः नित्यः अनित्यश्च ।<br>नित्यः परमाणुरूपः । अनित्यः कार्यरूपः । पुनः त्रिविधः<br>शरीरेन्द्रियविषय भेदात् । शरीरं वायुलोके । इन्द्रियं स्पर्शग्राहकं<br>त्वक् सर्वशरीरवर्ति । विषयो वृक्षादिकम्पनहेतुः । शरीरान्तः संचारी<br>वायुः प्राणः । स च एकोऽपि उपाधिभेदात् प्राणापानादिसंज्ञां<br>लभते ॥ ४ ॥
          - **commentaries**:
            - **Item 1**:
              - **author**: English Paraphrase
              - **commentary**: 4. Air is that which possesses touch but is without<br>colour. It is two-fold: eternal and non-eternal. The eternal<br>is of the nature of atom; the non-eternal is of the<br>nature of product. Again, it is three-fold; owing to<br>its classification into body, organ and object. Body is<br>found in the world of wind-god; organ is the tactile<br>organ by which one apprehends touch, and it is spread<br>over the whole body; object is the cause of tremor<br>of trees etc. The air that circulates within the body<br>is the vital breath. Though one, it is denoted variously<br>as prāṇa, apāna, etc owing to different situations.
            - **Item 2**:
              - **author**: Sanskrit Commentary
              - **commentary**: वायुं लक्षयति । रूपरहितेति ।<br>पृथिव्यादावतिव्याप्तिवारणाय रूपरहितेति । प्राणस्य कुत्रान्तर्भाव इत्यत आह । शरीरेति ।<br>स चेति । एक एव प्राणः स्थानभेदात्प्राणापानादिशब्दैः व्यवहियत इत्यर्थः । स्पर्शानुमेयो<br>आकाशादावतिव्याप्तिवारणाय स्पर्शवानिति । वायुः । तथा हि - योऽयं वायौ वाति सति अनुष्णाशीतस्पर्श उपलभ्यते स कचिदाश्रितः गुणत्वाद्रूपवत् । न चास्य आश्रयः पृथिवी उद्भूतस्पर्शवत्पार्थिवस्योद्भूत- रूपवत्त्वनियमात् । न जलतेजसी अनुष्णाशीतस्पर्शवत्त्वात् । न विभुचतुष्टयम् सर्वत्रोपलब्धिप्रसङ्गात् । न मनः परमाणुस्पर्शस्यातीन्द्रियत्वात् । तस्माद्यः प्रतीयमानस्पर्शाश्रयः स वायुः (एव) । ननु वायुः प्रत्यक्षः प्रत्यक्षस्पर्शाश्रयत्वात् घटवत् इति चेत् न । उद्भूतरूपस्योपाधित्वात् । 'यत्र द्रव्यत्वे सति बहिरिन्द्रियजन्यप्रत्यक्षत्वं, तत्र उद्भूतरूपवत्त्वम्' इति साध्यव्यापकत्वम् । पक्षे साधनाव्यापकत्वम् । न चैवं तप्तवारिस्थतेजसोऽपि अप्रत्यक्षत्वापत्तिः इष्टत्वात् । तस्माद्र्परहितत्वाद्वायुरप्रत्यक्षः । इदानीं कार्यरूपपृथिव्यादिचतुष्टयस्योत्पत्तिविनाशक्रमः कथ्यते । ईश्वरस्य चिकीर्षावशात्परमाणुषु क्रिया जायते । ततः परमाणुद्वयसंयोगे द्वयणुकमुत्पद्यते । त्रिभिरेव द्वयणुकैस्त्रयणुकमुत्पद्यते । एवं चतुरणुकादिक्रमेण महती पृथिवी; महत्य आपः, महत्तेजः, महान्वायुरुत्पद्यते । एवमुत्पन्नस्य कार्यद्रव्यस्य संजिहीर्षावशात् क्रियया परमाणुद्रव्यविभागे द्वयणुकनाशः । इत्येवं पृथिव्यादिनाशः । असमवायिकारणनाशात् द्वयणुकनाशः । समवायिकारणनाशात् त्र्यणुकनाश इति संप्रदायः सर्वत्रासमवायिकारणनाशात् द्रव्यनाश इति नवीनाः । किं पुनः परमाणुसद्भावे प्रमाणम् । उच्यते- जालसूर्यमरीचिस्थं सर्वतः सूक्ष्मतमं यत् द्रव्यं उपलभ्यते तत्सावयवं चाक्षुषद्रव्यत्वाद्धटवत् । त्र्यणुकावयवोऽपि सावयवः महदारम्भकत्वात्कपालवत् । यो द्वयणुकवयवः स परमाणुः । स च नित्यः, तस्यापि कार्यत्वे अनवस्थाप्रसङ्गात् । सृष्टिप्रल्यसद्भावे 'धाता यथापूर्वमकल्पयत् ।' इति श्रुतिरेव प्रमाणम् । 'सर्वकार्यद्रव्यध्वंसोऽवान्तरप्रल्यः । सर्वभावकार्यध्वंसो महाप्रलयः' इति विवेकः ।
            - **Item 3**:
              - **author**: English Translation
              - **commentary**: Dīpikā:<br>The characteristic mark of air is given in the Text: rūpa.... To remove overapplicability in ether etc air is defined as possessing touch. To remove overapplicability in earth etc it is defined as without colour. The question, wherein is the inclusion of vital air, is answered by the Text: In the body.... Vital Breath is only one; but owing to its different locations (within the body), and due to its different functions, it is known by various names as prāṇa, apāna etc.[31. Prāna, though one, is spoken of as five according to its<br>different locations and functions.<br>हृदि प्राणो गुदेऽपानः समानो नाभिसंस्थितः ।<br>उदानः कण्ठदेशस्थो व्यानः सर्वशरीरगः ॥<br>The Air that is inhaled and exhaled through the mouth and the<br>nostrils is Prāna, and is located in the heart. The air that presses<br>down water, waste matter, foetus etc is apāna and is located in<br>the anus. Some opine that it functions from the navel (nābhi-apanayanāt<br>mūtra purīsādeh apāno adhovitih vāyuh nabhisthānah). Samāna helps<br>in the digestion of food etc by stimulating gastric fire in the stomach<br>and is located in the region of the navel. Udāna takes the digested<br>food etc upward from the navel and which, located in the throat,<br>rises up the throat and enters into the head. Vyāna is the vital<br>air that courses through the entire nervous system and is diffused<br>through the whole body] Air is inferred by the sense of touch. The neither-hot-nor-cold touch that we feel when the wind blows must reside in some substance as it is a quality like colour (because of the universal principle that a quality always resides in a certain<br>substance); earth cannot be its (ie of touch) substratum; because,<br>as a rule, all earthy substances having manifested touch have<br>also manifested colour (while air has no manifested colour);<br>nor can it reside in water and light because it is neither<br>cold nor hot; nor can it reside in the four all-pervading substances<br>(ether, time, space and soul), for if it resides in them, then<br>it ought to be found everywhere; nor does it reside in mind,<br>because, if it did, then (the mind being atomic) touch residing<br>in atom (cannot be felt), it being beyond apprehension by<br>the senses. Therefore, that which is revealed to us as the<br>substratum of touch is air.<br>Objection: Air is visible, because, it is the substratum of<br>perceptible touch, like a jar.<br>Reply: It is wrong; because, of the defect of adventitious<br>condition (upādhi) of manifested colour. [32. Upādhi is defined as being pervasive of the thing to be proved<br>while not being pervasive of the reason. In a good syllogism that<br>which is vyāpaka to the thing to be proved (sādhya) must also<br>be vyāpaka to the reason (hetu or sādhana). If it is found to be<br>vyāpaka to sādhya but avyāpaka to sādhana, then it becomes a<br>bad hetu, suffering from the defect of upādhi] Here, in the argument,<br>Air is visible, because it is the substratum of perceptible touch,<br>the reason is defective owing to the necessary condition of<br>having manifested colour (for rendering a thing perceptible).<br>All substances possessing perceptibility produced by an external<br>sense organ have in them manifested colour, like a jar. Here,<br>manifested colour is pervasive of the thing to be proved (ie<br>perceptibility). But, manifested colour is not found wherever<br>there is the substratum of perceptible touch; here, there is<br>the non-pervasiveness of the reason in the subject. [33. That is, in air which is the subject here. It is a known<br>fact that air, though the substratum of perceptible touch, does not<br>possess manifested colour. So, this necessary condition of having<br>manifested colour does not extend to the reason: because it is the<br>substratum of perceptible touch. Therefore, the argument, air is visible<br>cannot be sustained by a reason vitiated by the defect of upadhi.<br>This is the idea] By this,<br>there should be no objection to the statement that the heat<br>that is present in hot water is imperceptible (because of<br>the above argument that only things possessing manifested<br>colour are perceptible); because that is desired by the Naiyāyikas.<br>Therefore, air is imperceptible, because it is devoid of colour.<br>Origin and Dissolution of the four Mahā Bhūtas:<br>Now is being explained the process of creation and<br>dissolution of the material universe produced from the four<br>tangible substances beginning with earth. Owing to the Creative<br>Will of the Omnipotent God, motion is first produced in<br>the atoms. Then, from the conjunction of two atoms a Dyad<br>(dvyanuka) is produced. Then, as a consequence of conjunction<br>of three Dyads, a Triad (tryanuka) is formed. Similarly, with<br>four Triads, a Quadrate (caturanaka) is produced, and so<br>on and on until the great masses of gross earth, water, light,<br>and atmosphere are formed. When the dissolution of the products<br>of substances thus created is desired by the Omnipotent Lord,<br>motion is produced dividing the monads. Owing to this, the<br>contact between two atoms is destroyed whereupon the<br>destruction of the Dyad takes place. The Dyad being destroyed,<br>there follows the disintegration of Triads, Quadrates and so<br>on until the entire created masses of earth etc are destroyed.<br>The traditional view is that due to the dissolution of the<br>non-intimate cause between the two atoms, a Dyad is destroyed.<br>Then, due to the destruction of the intimate cause, subsequent<br>products like the Triads etc are disintegrated. But the modern<br>Naiyāyikas hold the view that everywhere the disintegration<br>of the products of substances takes place as a result of<br>the dissolution of the union between two atoms owing to<br>the destruction of the non-intimate cause.<br>[34. Keeping in view the Vaiśeşika doctrine of recurrent creation<br>and dissolution, Annambhatta discusses here the origin and dissolution<br>of the four Mahābhūtas of gross Earth, gross Water, gross Tejas<br>and gross Air. Creation as also dissolution follows a set pattern.<br>But there is a divergence of views among the followers of the Vaiśeşika<br>Doctrine with regard to the operative cause that leads to the disintegration<br>of a Dyad and a Triad. The Traditional view is that the destruction<br>of asamavāyi kāraṇa between the two atoms leads to the disintegration<br>of a Dyad. Then, the destruction of Samavāyi Kāraṇa of Triads<br>(ie the destruction of the Dyads themselves which constitute the Samavāyi<br>Kāraṇa of a Triad) leads to the disintegration of Triads. Thus, first,<br>there takes place the destruction of asamavāyi kāraṇa between two<br>paramāņus; then, takes place the destruction of samavāyi kāraṇa.<br>According to the Navinas (Moderners), everywhere the destruction<br>of asamavāyi karana leads to the disintegration of gross effect substances.<br>Thus, the destruction of a triad is invariably preceded not only by<br>the destruction of the samavāyi kāraṇa (or the binary product) but<br>also by the destruction of asamavāyi kāraṇa between the two atoms]<br>Proof for the existence of atoms (Paramāņu):<br>What again is the proof of the existence of the atoms?<br>This is answered as follows: The finest particle of mote perceived<br>floating in a sunbeam is a structure consisting of component<br>parts as it is a substance which is visible to the eye, like<br>a cloth. Even a component part of a Triad (a Dyad) is<br>a composite whole made up of parts because it produces<br>the large magnitude (a Triad), just like a thread. [35. The argument goes like this:<br>(1) Every visible substance is composed of parts, eg a piece<br>of cloth which is composed of threads. The finest mote in the sunbeam<br>as it passes through a lattice window is a visible substance which<br>is the triad. Therefore it is composed of parts, that is, of dyads.<br>Here there is no instance to cite the contrary; as such it is quite<br>logical.<br>(2) Again the dyad too is composed of parts, viz, the atoms,<br>like a thread. Whatever produces a large object is composed of<br>parts, eg the threads in a cloth. A dyad generates a visible object<br>(like a triad). Therefore, a dyad is composed of parts. Here also,<br>there is no instance contrary to this argument. Hence it is not open<br>to any objection. Thus, thread in relation to cloth, and dyad in<br>relation to triad are the mahadārambhakas of the large magnitude,<br>like the cloth in the case of the former and triad in the latter<br>case. The conclusion is that on the strength of arguments above,<br>the existence of atoms is established] An atom<br>is that which forms a part of a dyad and it is eternal. Otherwise,<br>if we assume the atom also to be a product of still smaller<br>parts, it would result in the defect of endless regression.<br>And also the hypothesis that the mountain Meru and the<br>mustard seed are of equal size will remain unsolved. [36. Now, it may be argued that atom also is composed of parts<br>on the basis of earlier argument that whatever generates an effect,<br>is itself composed of parts, like the dyad, because the atoms produce<br>dyads. Annambhatta answers such arguments by saying that the argument<br>that the atom too is composed of parts, would land us in regression<br>ad infinitum (anavasthā) inasmuch as there would be an endless<br>series of generating causes which is absurd. Further, assumption of<br>a genesis of atoms compels us to assume infinite divisibility of a<br>material substance. If such be the case, then, a tiny mustard seed<br>would be as much an infinitely divisible thing as the largest mountain.<br>The difference in sizes between substances can be explained only<br>if the atom is accepted as the smallest unit not admitting of any<br>division. It is nothing but the greater or smaller number of atoms<br>that makes one thing bigger and another smaller. A thing like mountain<br>Meru is larger because it contains larger number of parts than a<br>mustard seed which is smaller to Meru because mustard seed contains<br>lesser number of parts. To calculate these numbers we must have<br>a common unit like an atom. If we do not recognize the atom<br>as an indivisible unit and, instead, go on dividing the atom ad infinitum,<br>then, the number of parts in Meru mountain and mustard seed will<br>be equal but the parts will vary in size and the question why one<br>is larger than the other will remain unresolved. This is solved thus:<br>A thing is larger or smaller according to the size of parts in them<br>are larger or smaller.]<br>Proof for creation and dissolution:<br>Question: What is the authority to establish the theory of<br>creation and dissolution?<br>Answer: The passages from the Vedic texts like: The Lord<br>created the world as in previous cycles, etc are the authority.<br>The destruction of all product substances beginning with binary<br>molecule up to the great mass of earth possessing the grossest<br>dimension etc is known as the intermediary dissolution. The<br>destruction of all positive categories is the great dissolution<br>or universal dissolution, mahāpralaya.[37. The Nyāya-Vaiśeṣika system, being an Orthodox System of<br>Thought, accepts vedic authority like other Orthodox Systems and<br>quotes the vedic passage as an authority to prove its contention<br>of recurrent creation and dissolution. Annambhaṭṭa mentions two kinds<br>of dissolution, avāntara pralaya and Mahāpralaya. In avāntara pralaya<br>all gross substances are destroyed leaving intact only the nityas like<br>the atoms, ākāśa, space, time, soul with their saṃskāras, and minds.<br>In Mahāpralaya all bhāva kāryas (positive effects) get destroyed. Only<br>imperishable substances like the paramāṇus (atoms) without their quality,<br>souls without their perishable saṃskāras, minds, ākāśa, space, and<br>time are left intact.]
        - **Item 14**:
          - **verse_number**: `14`
          - **original_text**: 5. Ākāśa:<br>शब्दगुणकमाकाशम् । तच्चैकं विभु नित्यञ्च ॥ ५ ॥
          - **commentaries**:
            - **Item 1**:
              - **author**: English Paraphrase
              - **commentary**: 5. Ākāśa is that which is characterised by the<br>distinctive quality of sound. And it is one, all-pervading,<br>and eternal.
            - **Item 2**:
              - **author**: Sanskrit Commentary
              - **commentary**: आकाशं लक्षयति । शब्दगुणकमिति । नन्वाकाशमपि पृथिव्यादिवन्नाना, किं नेत्याह ।<br>तच्चैकमिति । भेदे प्रमाणाभावादित्यर्थः । एकत्वादेव सर्वत्र<br>शब्दोपलब्धेर्विभुत्वमङ्गीकर्तव्यमित्याह विभ्विति । सर्वमूर्तद्रव्यसंयोगित्वं विभुत्वं, मूर्तत्वं<br>परिच्छिन्नपरिमाणवत्त्वं क्रियावत्त्वं वा । विभुत्वादेव आत्मवन्नित्यमित्याह । नित्यं<br>चेति ।
            - **Item 3**:
              - **author**: English Translation
              - **commentary**: Dīpikā:<br>Ākāśa is being indicated by the Text: Śabda.... The question<br>whether ether also is many like the earth etc is answered<br>by the Text: tat ca ekam and that is one. The implied<br>idea is that no diversity can be accepted in ākāśa for lack<br>of proof. Sound being perceived everywhere, it is one, and<br>all-pervading. This is stated by the Text: vibhu. Contact with<br>all corporeal objects is all-pervasion, Corporeality is the quality<br>of having definite dimensions; or, it is that possessing motion.<br>Being all-pervasive, ākāśa is also eternal like the soul.[38. For want of a more appropriate term for ākāśa, it is translated<br>here as ether. Multiplicity in ākāśa is not admitted since it is a<br>continuum and statements such as this ākāśa or that ākāśa are due<br>to the delimiting factors in relation to ākāśa. This cannot be a ground<br>to postulate multiplicity in ākāśa which is a unitary entity]
        - **Item 15**:
          - **verse_number**: `15`
          - **original_text**: 6. Time:<br>अतीतादिव्यवहारहेतुः कालः । स चैको विभुर्नित्यश्च ॥ ६ ॥
          - **commentaries**:
            - **Item 1**:
              - **author**: English Paraphrase
              - **commentary**: 6. Time is the special cause of conventional<br>expression of words like past etc and it is one,<br>all-pervading, and eternal.
            - **Item 2**:
              - **author**: Sanskrit Commentary
              - **commentary**: कालं लक्षयति । अतीतेति । सर्वाधारः कालः सर्वकार्यनिमित्तकारणम् ।
            - **Item 3**:
              - **author**: English Translation
              - **commentary**: Dīpikā:<br>Time is being indicated by the text: Atita. Time is the<br>substratum of everything and is also the instrumental cause<br>of all effects.[39. The Text defines 'Time' as atīta etc to avoid ativyāpti in<br>ghaṭa etc. Everything exists in relation to time and space. So if<br>time is merely defined as the cause of conventional expression, then<br>ativyāpti occurs in ghaṭa also, since ghaṭa is the cause of conventional<br>expression of the word ghaṭa. To avoid this, atītādi is prefixed to<br>the definition. Time comes to bear the terms like past, present,<br>and future under certain conditions, though time is only one. Also,<br>Kāla has no perceivable quality though a dravya]
        - **Item 16**:
          - **verse_number**: `16`
          - **original_text**: 7. Dik (space or direction):<br>प्राच्यादिव्यवहारहेतुर्दिक् । सा चैका विभ्वी नित्या च ॥ ७ ॥
          - **commentaries**:
            - **Item 1**:
              - **author**: English Paraphrase
              - **commentary**: 7. Direction is the cause of conventional expressions<br>like east etc and is one, all-pervading, and eternal.
            - **Item 2**:
              - **author**: Sanskrit Commentary
              - **commentary**: दिशो लक्षणमाह । प्राचीति । दिगपि कार्यमात्रनिमित्तकारणम् ।
            - **Item 3**:
              - **author**: English Translation
              - **commentary**: Dīpikā:<br>The text defines direction as prācī.... Direction is also<br>the instrumental cause of all effects.[40. Though dik is one only, it is indicated as east, west, etc in relation to the position of the sun. Space in the direction of<br>udayācala is known as east, in the direction of astācala is known<br>as west, in the direction of the Meru is known as north, and in<br>the direction opposite to the Meru is known as south. Like time<br>and ether, Dik (direction) also is inferred]
        - **Item 17**:
          - **verse_number**: `17`
          - **original_text**: 8. Ātmā (Soul):<br>ज्ञानाधिकरणमात्मा । स द्विविधः परमात्मा जीवात्मा च।<br>तत्रेश्वरः सर्वज्ञः परमात्मैक एव । जीवात्मा प्रतिशरीरं भिन्नो<br>विभुर्नित्यश्च ॥ ८ ॥
          - **commentaries**:
            - **Item 1**:
              - **author**: English Paraphrase
              - **commentary**: 8. The soul is the substratum of knowledge. It is two-fold: the supreme soul and the individual soul. Of these, the supreme soul is omnipotent and omniscient<br>and one only. The individual soul is different in each<br>body, is all-pervading, and eternal.
            - **Item 2**:
              - **author**: Sanskrit Commentary
              - **commentary**: आत्मनो लक्षणमाह । ज्ञानेति । आत्मानं विभजते । स द्विविध इति । परमात्मनो<br>लक्षणमाह । तत्रेति । नित्यज्ञानाधिकरणत्वमीश्वरत्वम् । नन्वीश्वरसद्भावे किं प्रमाणम् ।<br>न तावत्प्रत्यक्षम् । तद्धि बाह्यमान्तरं वा । नाद्यः अरूपिद्रव्यत्वात् । न द्वितीयः<br>आत्मसुखदुःखादिव्यतिरिक्तत्वात् । नाप्यनुमानं लिङ्गाभावादिति चेत् न । अङ्करादिकं<br>सकर्तृकं कार्यत्वाद्धटवत् इत्यनुमानस्यैव प्रमाणत्वात् । उपादानगोचरापरोक्ष-<br>ज्ञानचिकीर्षाकृतिमत्त्वं कर्तृत्वम् ।<br>उपादानं समवायिकारणम् ।<br>सकलपरमाण्वादिसूक्ष्मदर्शित्वात्सर्वज्ञत्वम् । यः सर्वज्ञः स सर्ववित् इत्यागमोऽपि तत्र<br>प्रमाणम् । जीवस्य लक्षणमाह । जीव इति । सुखाद्याश्रयत्वं जीवलक्षणम् । ननु<br>मनुष्योऽहं ब्राह्मणोऽहम् इत्यादौ सर्वत्राहंप्रत्यये शरीरस्यैव विषयत्वाच्छरीरमेवात्मेति<br>चेत् न । शरीरस्यात्मत्वे करपादादिनाशे शरीरनाशादात्मनोऽपि नाशप्रसंगात् ।<br>नापीन्द्रियाणामात्मत्वम्, 'योऽहं घटमद्राक्षं सोऽहमिदानीं स्पृशामि'<br>इत्यनुसन्धानाभावप्रसङ्गात् । अन्यानुभूतेऽर्थे<br>अन्यस्यानुसंधानायोगात् ।<br>तस्माद्देहेन्द्रियव्यतिरिक्तो जीवः सुखदुःखादिवैचित्र्यात्प्रतिशरीरं भिन्नः । स च न परमाणुः ।<br>सर्वशरीरख्यापिसुखाद्यनुपलब्धिप्रसङ्गात् । न मध्यमपरिमाणवान् तथा सति अनित्यत्वप्रसङ्गेन<br>कृतहानाकृताभ्यागमप्रसङ्गात् । तस्मान्नित्यो विभुर्जीवः ।।
            - **Item 3**:
              - **author**: English Translation
              - **commentary**: Dīpikā:<br>The characteristic mark of the soul is defined by the<br>Text: jñāna.. Again, the text divides it: sa dvividhah.... The<br>Text tatra seeks to define the characteristic mark of the<br>supreme soul. Lordlines consists in being the substratum of<br>eternal knowledge.<br>Objection: What is the proof for the existence of Iśvara?<br>Perception cannot be the proof. If, however, perception is<br>presumed to be the proof, then, is it external perception<br>(ie perceivable by the external sense-organ, the eye) or is<br>it internal perception (ie perceived by the mind)? Not the<br>first, because, He is a substance without colour, nor could<br>He be the latter, because He is distinct from the feelings<br>of pain, pleasure, etc felt by the individual soul; nor can<br>it be said that He can be inferred, owing to lack of similar<br>instance to support the inference; nor the Vedic testimony<br>(can prove His existence) for lack of Vedic texts establishing<br>His existence.<br>Reply: No; it is not so; because earth, sprouts etc are<br>caused by some agent since they are products like a jar.<br>Thus, the existence of Iśvara is proved by inference. Agent<br>is one who possesses an immediate knowledge of the inherent<br>causal apparatus, a will to act, and an effort. Inherent cause<br>is the material cause. Omniscience consists in possessing a<br>direct knowledge of all subtle substances, atoms etc. Vedic<br>texts like, He who is the Omniscient is also the immediate<br>knower of everything etc are the proofs to establish the existence<br>of Iśvara.<br>The text gives the characteristic mark of the individual<br>soul: jīva.... The characteristic mark of the human soul consists<br>in its being the abode of pleasure, pain, etc.<br>Objection: This body itself is the soul, because, everywhere,<br>the body itself is taken to be the object of the consciousness<br>I when one says, I am a man, I am a brāhmaņa, etc.<br>Reply: It is not so; if body be the soul, then the inevitable<br>destruction of the soul has to be accepted when the body<br>is destroyed with the destruction of hands, feet, etc. Nor<br>can the sense organs be the soul, because in that case,<br>there cannot occur the recollection I who saw the pot is the<br>same I now touching it; for, what was experienced by one<br>in the past cannot be recollected by another. Therefore, the<br>soul is quite distinct from the body and the organs. Also,<br>(we have to admit) that there are as many human souls<br>as there are bodies for the reason of variety of experiences<br>of pleasure, pain, etc (as otherwise we cannot account for<br>the variety of experiences of happiness, misery, etc in those<br>bodies).
