        - **Item 99**:
          - **verse_number**: `99`
          - **original_text**: 12. Pain:<br>सर्वेषां प्रतिकूलतया वेदनीयं दुःखम् ॥ १२ ॥<br>13. Desire etc:<br>इच्छा कामः । क्रोधो द्वेषः । कृतिः प्रयत्नः । विहितकर्मजन्यो<br>धर्मः । निषिद्धकर्मजन्यस्त्वधर्मः ॥ १३ ॥<br>14. Eight qualities beginning with Buddhi:<br>बुध्यादयोऽष्टावात्ममात्रविशेषगुणाः । बुद्धीच्छा प्रयत्ना<br>द्विविधाः । नित्या अनित्याश्च । नित्या ईश्वरस्य अनित्या<br>जीवस्य ॥ १४ ॥
          - **commentaries**:
            - **Item 1**:
              - **author**: English Paraphrase
              - **commentary**: 12. That which is experienced by all with disagreable<br>feelings is pain.<br>13. Wish is desire; ill-feeling is anger; volitional<br>effort is the will-to-do; merit is that which is born<br>of enjoined actions; but demerit is that which is born<br>of prohibited actions.<br>14. The eight qualities beginning with buddhi are<br>the specific qualities of the soul only. Cognition, desire,<br>and effort are of two kinds: eternal and non-eternal.<br>Eternals belong to Iśvara; non-eternals belong to the<br>human soul.<br>[123. Conjunction and some other qualities like numericals of two<br>etc also reside in many, but they are not eternal. So, the term<br>nitya in the definition of generality (or universal) excludes them.<br>The atom is eternal and resides in many; but it is not one residing<br>in many, so, by the term aneka in the definition, ativyāpti in atom<br>is avoided. The absolute negation is however eternal, one, and resides<br>in many. Therefore, the word anugatam in the text must be interpreted<br>to mean, samavetam, ie existing in many in inherent relation. This<br>interpretation excludes absolute negation which does not reside in<br>things by the relation of inherence. According to Kanāda, it is the<br>universal called the Sattā Jāti that produces the notion of existence<br>in the case of the first three categories, viz substance, quality and<br>action. Sāmānya is a common general feature residing in things by<br>the relation of inherence. As jāti, it is the eternal non-particular<br>real abiding in many substances simultaneously; hence it is one.<br>Cows are many and variegated but cowness (in cow or blueness<br>in a quality like blue) are the common features found in many particulars<br>like cow and blue colour which get destroyed after sometime; but<br>their jāti (cowness in case of cow, bluenss in case of blue) neither<br>originated nor gets dissolved; this universal feature is the same in<br>all the substances; hence it is a unitary principle. This is found<br>to exist in the first three categories.<br>124. Viśesa is the fifth Padārtha in the Nyāya-Vaiśeşika system.<br>It resides in the atoms and other eternal substances such as ākāśa<br>(ether), dik (space), kāla (time), soul and manas for the purpose<br>of differentiating one from the other. According to this School of<br>Thought, there is need for a differentiating agency like the viśeșa<br>in case of atoms which have similar qualities and the same universal]

        - **Item 100**:
          - **verse_number**: `100`
          - **original_text**: 15. Samskāra:<br>संस्कारस्त्रिविधः । वेगो भावना स्थितिस्थापकश्चेति । वेगः<br>पृथिव्यादिचतुष्टयमनोवृत्तिः । अनुभवजन्या स्मृतिहेतुर्भावना ।<br>आत्ममात्रवृत्तिः । अन्यथाकृतस्य पुनस्तदवस्थापकः<br>स्थितिस्थापकः कटादिपृथिवीवृत्तिः ॥ १५ ॥
          - **commentaries**:
            - **Item 1**:
              - **author**: English Paraphrase
              - **commentary**: 15. Impression is of three kinds: velocity, reminiscent<br>impression and elasticity. Velocity resides in four<br>substances beginning with earth, and in mind. That<br>which is born of experience and which causes recollection,<br>is reminiscent impression. It resides in the soul only.<br>Elasticity is the force that brings a thing back to its<br>normal shape whenever it is distorted. It resides in<br>mat etc which are the transformations of earth.
            - **Item 2**:
              - **author**: Sanskrit Commentary
              - **commentary**: संस्कारं विभजते — संस्कार इति ॥ संस्कारत्वजातिमान्संस्कारः । वेगस्याश्रयमाह<br>वेग इति ॥ वेगत्वजातिमान्वेगः । भावनां लक्षयति — अनुभवेति ॥<br>अनुभवध्वंसेऽति व्याप्तिवारणाय स्मृतीति । आत्मादावतिव्याप्तिवारणाय अनुभवेति ।<br>स्मृतेरपि संस्कारजनकत्वं नवीनैरुक्तम् । स्थितिरथापकं लक्षयति — अन्यथेति ॥<br>संख्यादयोऽष्टौ नैमित्तिकद्रवत्ववेगस्थितिस्थापकाः सामान्यगुणाः । अन्ये रूपादयो<br>विशेषगुणाः । द्रव्यविभाजकोपाधिद्वयसमानाधिकरणावृत्तिजातिमद्गुणत्वं विशेषगुणत्वम् ।
            - **Item 3**:
              - **author**: English Translation
              - **commentary**: Dīpikā:<br>The Text divides impression: samskāra.... Impression is<br>that which possesses its generic attribute impressionness. The<br>Text indicates the substratum of velocity: vega.... Velocity is<br>that which possesses the generic attribute velocityness (vegatva).<br>The Text defines reminiscent impression: anubhava.... To avoid<br>the defect of overapplicability in soul etc reminiscent impression<br>is defined as born of experience. To avoid overapplicability<br>in destruction of experience, the definition is qualified with<br>the adjunct, born of memory. Moderners are of the opinion<br>that memory is born of impression. The Text defines elasticity:<br>anyatha.... The eight qualities beginning with number, occasional<br>fluidity, velocity, and elasticity are the general qualities. Other<br>qualities like colour etc are special qualities. The property<br>of being a special quality consists in possessing the genus<br>which does not exist in one which exists in a substratum in<br>which two upadhis that divide dravya also exist.
        - **Item 101**:
          - **verse_number**: `101`
          - **original_text**: 16. Karma:<br>चलनात्मकं कर्म । ऊर्ध्वदेशसंयोगहेतुरुत्क्षेपणम् । अधोदेश-<br>संयोगहेतुरपक्षेपणम् । शरीरसंनिकृष्टसंयोगहेतुराकुञ्चनम् । विप्र-<br>कृष्टसंयोगहेतुः प्रसारणम् । अन्यत् सर्वं गमनम् । पृथिव्या-<br>दिचतुष्टयमनोमात्रवृत्ति ॥ १६ ॥
          - **commentaries**:
            - **Item 1**:
              - **author**: English Paraphrase
              - **commentary**: 16. Action is of the nature of motion. That which<br>causes connection with regions upward is tossing; that<br>which causes connection with regions downwards is<br>dropping; that which causes connection nearer the body<br>is contraction; that which causes connection with distant<br>regions is expansion. All other varieties of motion is<br>Motion. It resides in the four substances beginning with<br>earth, and in mind.
            - **Item 2**:
              - **author**: Sanskrit Commentary
              - **commentary**: कर्मणो लक्षणमाह चलनेति ॥ उत्क्षेपणादीनां कार्यभेदमाह ऊध्र्वेति ॥<br>शरीरिति । वक्रतासंपादकं आकुञ्चनम् । ऋजुतासंपादकं प्रसारणमित्यर्थः ।
            - **Item 3**:
              - **author**: English Translation
              - **commentary**: Dīpikā:<br>The Text defines action: calana.... Contraction is the action<br>that causes the body to bend. Similarly, expansion is the<br>action that causes the straightening of the body etc.
        - **Item 102**:
          - **verse_number**: `102`
          - **original_text**: 17.<br>नित्यमेकमनेकानुगतं सामान्यं द्रव्यगुणकर्मवृत्ति । तद्विविधं<br>पराऽपरभेदात् । परं सत्ता । अपरं द्रव्यत्वादिः ॥ १७ ॥
          - **commentaries**:
            - **Item 1**:
              - **author**: English Paraphrase
              - **commentary**: 17. That which is eternal, one, and which resides<br>in many things is the universal. It resides in substance,<br>quality and action. It is twofold due to its division<br>into the more extensive and the less extensive. Existence
            - **Item 2**:
              - **author**: Sanskrit Commentary
              - **commentary**: सामान्यं लक्षयति नित्यमिति ॥ संयोगेऽतिव्याप्तिवारणाय नित्यमिति । जलपरमाणुगतरूपेऽतिव्याप्तिवारणाय एकेति । परमाणुपरिमाणादावतिव्याप्तिवारणाय अनेकेति । अनुगतत्वं समवेतत्वम् । तेन नाभावादावतिव्याप्तिः ।
            - **Item 3**:
              - **author**: English Translation
              - **commentary**: Dīpikā:<br>The Text defines Universal: nitya.... To avoid overapplicability in samyoga, the term Nitya is added. To avoid overapplicability in the form in the atom of water, the term eka is added. To avoid overapplicability in the dimension of an atom, the term aneka is added. Anugatatva is the quality of residing in many by inherent relation. By this, overapplicability in negation etc is avoided.
        - **Item 103**:
          - **verse_number**: `103`
          - **original_text**: 18. Viśeṣa<br>नित्यद्रव्यवृत्तयो व्यावर्तका विशेषाः ॥ १८ ॥

            - **Item 3**:

        - **Item 104**:
          - **verse_number**: `104`
          - **original_text**: 19. Samavāyah<br>नित्यसम्बन्धः समवायः । अयुतसिद्धवृत्तिः । ययोर्द्वयोर्मध्ये एकमविनश्यदपराऽश्रितमेवावतिष्ठते तावयुतसिद्धौ यथा<br>अवयवाऽवयविनौ गुणगुणिनौ क्रियाक्रियावन्तौ जातिव्यक्ती<br>विशेषनित्यद्रव्ये चेति ॥ १९ ॥
          - **commentaries**:
            - **Item 1**:
              - **author**: English Paraphrase
              - **commentary**: 19. Inherence is the eternal relation; it exists in<br>an inseparable pair: when, between two things, one<br>thing, as long as it is not destroyed, exists in the<br>other thing only, they are known as inseparable pairs;<br>for example, part and the whole; quality and the qualified;<br>motion and the moving object; genus and the individual;<br>and particular and the eternal substance.
            - **Item 2**:
              - **author**: Sanskrit Commentary
              - **commentary**: समवायं लक्षयति नित्येति ।। संयोगेऽतिव्याप्तिवारणाय नित्येति ।<br>आकाशादावतिव्याप्तिवारणाय संबन्धेति । अयुतसिद्धलक्षणमाह - ययोरिति \|\| 'नीलो<br>घटः' इति विशिष्टप्रतीतिर्विशेषणविशेष्यसंबन्धविषया, विशिष्टबुद्धित्वात्, दण्डीतिविशिष्ट-<br>बुद्धिवत् इति समवायसिद्धिः । अवयवावयविनाविति ॥ द्रव्यसमवायिकारणमवयवः<br>जन्यद्रव्यमवयवि ।
            - **Item 3**:
              - **author**: English Translation
              - **commentary**: Dīpikā:<br>The Text defines inherence: nitya.... To avoid<br>overapplicability in conjunction, nitya is added to the definition<br>(because in conjunction also there is connection of two halves,<br>as in a jar; but it can be destroyed at any moment by<br>separation; so it is not nitya). To avoid overapplicability in<br>ether etc relation is added to the definition; ether is an<br>eternal substance, but it is not a sambandha. Inseparable pair<br>is explained in the Text: yayoh.... The knowledge which<br>apprehends the objects with adjuncts like blue jar apprehends<br>the relation between the attribute and the thing possessing<br>that attribute; because, it is a knowledge of the qualified<br>and the attribute like the attributive knowledge: a man with<br>a stick. Thus inherence is proved. The part is the inherent<br>cause of the whole. The substance produced of those parts<br>is the composite whole. <br>[125. Samavāya is the sixth padārtha in the Vaiśeşika system.<br>Ayuta siddhi is the relation between two things as long as the parts<br>are in the whole, eg threads which bring into existence a piece<br>of cloth. Here, threads are the parts; the cloth is the whole. Threads<br>are independent of the cloth, but the cloth is not independent of<br>threads, as the cloth exists only in the threads; this relation between<br>the two is Ayuta siddhi and the related things are Ayuta siddha.<br>Similarly, the relation between the quality and the qualified, like<br>the red colour which is a quality (guna) existing in a substance<br>like a flower. Though a substance can exist independently, quality<br>cannot exist apart from the substance; so, they are Ayuta siddha<br>inasmuch as a quality, as long as it lasts, has to subsist in a substance.<br>Similar is the relation between action and substance of which it<br>is an action. The ayuta siddhi relation between jāti and vyakti is<br>the fourth one. Individual cows cannot exist independent of the universal<br>cowness which can exist independent of particular cows. Therefore,<br>they are ayuta siddha. Lastly, the relation of mutual inseparability<br>between višesa and eternal substance. They are ayuta siddha for the<br>reason that things related are themselves eternal entities]
        - **Item 105**:
          - **verse_number**: `105`
          - **original_text**: 20. Antecedent Negation:<br>अनादिः सान्तः प्रागभावः । उत्पत्तेः पूर्वं कार्यस्य ॥ २० ॥
          - **commentaries**:
            - **Item 1**:
              - **author**: English Paraphrase
              - **commentary**: 20. Antecedent negation is without a beginning but<br>with an end; it exists prior to the production of an<br>effect.
            - **Item 2**:
              - **author**: Sanskrit Commentary
              - **commentary**: प्रागभावं लक्षयति अनादिरिति ॥ आकाशादावतिव्याप्ति वारणाय सान्त इति ।<br>घटादावतिव्याप्तिवारणाय अनादिरिति । प्रतियोगिसमवायिकारणवृत्तिः प्रतियोगिजनको<br>भविष्यतीति व्यवहारहेतुः प्रागभावः ।
            - **Item 3**:
              - **author**: English Translation
              - **commentary**: Dīpikā:<br>The Text explains antecedent negation: anādi.... To avoid<br>overapplicability in ether etc the term with an end is added<br>to the definition; (because though ether is anādi it has no<br>destruction). To exclude jar etc from the definition, the term<br>without a beginning is added to the definition; (because, jar<br>etc have a beginning and also an end). The cause of its<br>counter correlative (ie abhāva) resides in the intimate cause<br>of its counter correlative (ie the negation of jar resides in<br>its material cause, the atoms of clay). Antecedent non-existence<br>is the cause of such usage of words like: Will come into<br>existence.
        - **Item 106**:
          - **verse_number**: `106`
          - **original_text**: 21. Destruction:<br>सादिरनन्तः प्रध्वंसः । उत्पत्यनन्तरं कार्यस्य ॥ २१ ॥
          - **commentaries**:
            - **Item 1**:
              - **author**: English Paraphrase
              - **commentary**: 21. Destruction has a beginning but is without an<br>end; it occurs after the production of an effect.
            - **Item 2**:
              - **author**: Sanskrit Commentary
              - **commentary**: ध्वंसं लक्षयति सादिरिति ॥ घटादावतिव्याप्तिवारणाय अनन्तेति ।<br>आकाशादावतिव्याप्तिवारणाय सादिरिति । प्रतियोगिजन्यः प्रतियोगिसमवायिकारणवृत्तिर्ध्वस्त<br>इति व्यवहारहेतुः ध्वंसः ।
            - **Item 3**:
              - **author**: English Translation
              - **commentary**: Dīpikā:<br>The Text defines destruction: Sādi.... To exclude jar etc<br>ananta is added to the definition. To avert overapplicaibility<br>in space etc sadih is added. It is produced by its counter<br>correlative and resides in the intimate cause of its own counter<br>correlative. Pradhvamsa is the cause of usage of words like<br>it is destroyed.
        - **Item 107**:
          - **verse_number**: `107`
          - **original_text**: 22. Absolute Negation:<br>त्रैकालिकसंसर्गावच्छिन्नप्रतियोगिताकोऽत्यन्ताभावः । यथा भूतले<br>घटो नास्तीति ॥ २२ ॥
          - **commentaries**:
            - **Item 1**:
              - **author**: English Paraphrase
              - **commentary**: 22. Absolute negation exists in all the three times,<br>having that which ascertains or reflects counter correlative<br>delimited by relation or connection, as in the statement:<br>There is no jar on this ground.
            - **Item 2**:
              - **author**: Sanskrit Commentary
              - **commentary**: अत्यन्ताभावं लक्षयति — त्रैकालिकेति ॥ अन्योन्याभावेऽतिव्याप्तिवारणाय संसर्गेति ।<br>ध्वंसप्रागभावयोरतिव्याप्तिवारणाय त्रैकालिकेति ।
            - **Item 3**:
              - **author**: English Translation
              - **commentary**: Dīpikā:<br>The Text defines absolute negation: Traikālika.... To avoid<br>overapplicability in reciprocal negation, the term<br>samsargā-vacchinna is added to the definition. (ie pratiyogitā<br>is delimited by samsarga which is the relation other than the<br>relation of identity). To avert overapplicability in antecedent<br>and destructive negations, the term traikālika is added to<br>the definition. <br>[126. That to which negation occurs and which is the counter<br>correlative to its negation may be termed as pratiyogi. The characteristic<br>attribute in that pratiyogi, is pratiyogita, or pratiyogitvam. Pot is a<br>pratiyogi, because non-existence or negation may occur to it, and<br>also because it becomes the counter correlative to its abhāva. When<br>pot becomes the pratiyogi, it possesses pratiyogita. When we say,<br>pratiyogi pot does not exist, the pratiyogita residing in the pratiyogi<br>pot is delimited by the adjunct potness. The knowledge that cloth<br>does not exist happens when pratiyogita, residing in the pratiyogi cloth<br>becomes delimited by the adjunct clothness. Similarly, when we say,<br>there is antecedent negation of pot in the earth, the pratiyogita in<br>the pot will be delimited by the adjunct, viz relation of time prior<br>to the birth of the pot. And, when we say, Pot does not exist<br>in all the three times, pratiyogita in the pot should be delimited<br>by the adjunct, viz relation of time pertaining to past, present and<br>future. When pratiyogita is delimited by the relation of all the three<br>times, there happens absolute negation. That is to say, atyanta-abhāva<br>is that to which pratiyogi, does not exist at all]
        - **Item 108**:
          - **verse_number**: `108`
          - **original_text**: 23. Reciprocal Negation:<br>तादात्म्यसम्बन्धावच्छिन्नप्रतियोगिताकोऽन्योन्याभावः । यथा घटः<br>पटो नेति ॥ २३ ॥
          - **commentaries**:
            - **Item 1**:
              - **author**: English Paraphrase
              - **commentary**: 23. That which ascertains or reflects counter<br>correlative as delimited by the relation of identity is<br>reciprocal negation, eg the statement: jar is not cloth.
            - **Item 2**:
              - **author**: Sanskrit Commentary
              - **commentary**: अन्योन्याभावं लक्षयति<br>प्यसंसर्गभेदादेकप्रतियोगिकयोरत्यन्तान्योन्याभावयोर्भिन्नत्वम् । केवलदेवदत्ताभावादण्डय-<br>भावप्रतीत्या विशिष्टाभावः, 'एकसत्त्वेऽपि द्वौ न स्तः' इति प्रतीत्या द्वित्वावच्छिन्नाभावः,<br>संयोगेन घटवति समवायेन घटाभावः, तत्तद्धटाभावाद्धटत्त्वावच्छिन्नप्रतियोगि-<br>ताकसामान्याभावश्चातिरिक्तः । एवमन्योन्याभावोऽपि । घटत्वेन पटो नास्तीति प्रतीत्या<br>व्यधिकरणधर्मावच्छिन्नाभावो नाङ्गीक्रियते । पटे घटत्वं नास्तीति तदर्थः । अतिरिक्तत्वे<br>स केवलान्वयी । सामयिकाभावोऽप्यत्यन्ताभाव एव समयविशेषे प्रतीयमानः । घटाभाववति<br>घटानयने अत्यन्ताभावस्य अन्यत्र गमनाभावेऽपि अप्रतीतेः, घटापसरणे सति प्रतीतेः,<br>भूतलघटसंयोगप्रागभावध्वंसयो- र्घटात्यन्ताभावप्रतीतिनियामकत्वं कल्प्यते । घटवति<br>तत्संयोगप्रागभावध्वंसयोरसत्त्वादेवात्यन्ताभावस्याप्रतीतिः । घटापसरणे तु संयोगध्वंसस्य<br>सत्त्वात्प्रतीतिरिति । केवलाधिकरणेनैव नास्तीति व्यवहारोपपत्तौ अभावो न पदार्थान्तरमिति<br>तादात्म्येति ।। प्रतियोगितावच्छेदकारो-गुरुः । तत् न । अभावानङ्गीकारे कैवल्यस्य निर्वक्तुमाशक्यत्वात् । अभावाभावो भाव एव । नातिरिक्तः, अनवस्था-प्रसङ्गात् । ध्वंसप्रागभावः प्रागभावध्वंसश्च प्रतियोग्येवेति प्राञ्चः । अभावाभावोऽतिरिक्त एव तृतीयाभावस्य प्रथमाभावरूपत्वान्नानवस्थेति नवीनाः ।
            - **Item 3**:
              - **author**: English Translation
              - **commentary**: Dīpikā:<br>The Text defines reciprocal negation: Tādātmya.... Absolute negation and reciprocal negation, though having one counter correlative, are manifold on account of the variety of the properties and connections that limit pratiyogita in the counter correlatives in each case. (That is, the number of reciprocal negation depends on the varieties of aropya, ie the properties that delimit pratiyogita in the counter correlatives and the varieties of absolute negation depend on the varieties of relation that delimit the pratiyogita in the counter correlative).<br>Even when Devadatta possessing a stick is found to exist, the non-existence of Devadatta associated with stick is accepted in the sense that there does not exist Devadatta without possessing a stick. To the question, 'Does Devadatta without possessing a stick exist?', we will have to reply in the negative even though there does exist Devadatta possessing a stick. Non-existence of mere Devadatta without possessing a stick is different from non-existence of Devadatta holding a stick even though pratiyogi Devadatta remains to be the same. Difference is due to attributes given to pratiyogita.<br>Even when one of the two things exists it is possible to say that two do not exist, because of the non-existence of the other one. The cognition that two do not exist consequent on supplying the attribute two-ness as adjunct to pratiyogitā residing in two is different from the knowledge two do not exist consequent on supplying the attribute one-ness as adjunct to pratiyogita residing in two. Though in the above two places pratiyogi happens to be the same, the negation having the same pratiyogi becomes manifold in accordance with various attributes to pratiyogita. The absence of the either of two or the absence of both becomes responsible for the knowledge that two do not exist.<br>In a place where there is a jar in the relation of conjunction,<br>the absence of jar in the relation of inherent union is found.<br>The negation of jar when pratiyogitā is limited by mere jarness<br>is different from the negation of jar, when the pratiyogitā<br>is limited by its special attributes. Similar is the case with<br>regard to reciprocal negation too. The negation of counter<br>correlative limited by vyadhikaraņa dharma (two attributes not<br>existing in the same substratum) which arises when one says,<br>cloth does not exist as having jarness in its inherent relation<br>is not accepted by Annambhatta. The meaning is that jar-ness<br>does not exist in cloth. If it is separate, then, it should<br>not be counter correlative to absolute negation. Periodical<br>negation also is the same as absolute negation because of<br>negation being apprehended every now and then. If one brings<br>a pot to a place where there is the negation of a jar, the<br>atyantābhāva does not leave the place. We have accordingly<br>to admit a rule that antecedent negation of the contact of<br>pot in the spot or destruction of the pot in the spot is<br>responsible for the perception of the absolute negation existing<br>there.<br>The followers of Prabhakara say that abhāva is not a<br>separate category; because, the negation of a thing must be<br>explained with reference to the substratum. This is not so.<br>Without accepting negation, the mere-ness of substratum cannot<br>be explained. The absence of negation is existence; and this<br>is not separate from existence, as it involves the defect of<br>regressus ad infinitum. The ancients are of the opinion that<br>the antecedent negation of destruction and the destruction<br>of antecedent negation have the same counter correlative (ie<br>a jar).<br>The absence of non-existence is different from existence.<br>The modern Naiyāyikas say that the defect of regressus ad<br>infinitum is avoided by accepting the trtīyābhāva as similar<br>to prathamābhāva.
        - **Item 109**:
          - **verse_number**: `109`
          - **original_text**: SECTION X<br>CONCLUSION<br>सर्वेषां पदार्थानां यथायथमुक्तेष्वन्तर्भावात् सप्तैव पदार्था इति<br>सिद्धम् ॥ २४ ॥
          - **commentaries**:
            - **Item 1**:
              - **author**: English Paraphrase
              - **commentary**: 24. Since all categories are included severally in<br>those enumerated above, it is proved that categories<br>are only seven.
            - **Item 2**:
              - **author**: Sanskrit Commentary
              - **commentary**: ननु "प्रमाणप्रमेयसंशयप्रयोजनदृष्टान्तसिद्धान्तावयवतर्कनिर्णयवादजल्प वितण्डाहेत्वाभा-<br>तत्त्वज्ञानान्निश्श्रेयसाधिगमः"<br>इति न्यायसूत्रे<br>सच्छलजातिनिग्रहस्थानानां<br>षोडशपदार्थानामुक्तत्वात्कथं सप्तैवेत्यत आह<br>सर्वेषामिति ॥ सर्वेषां सप्तस्वेवान्तर्भाव<br>इत्यर्थः । 'आत्मशरीरन्द्रियार्थबुद्धिमनः प्रवृत्तिदोषप्रेत्यभावफलदुःखापवर्गास्तु प्रमेयम्' इति<br>द्वादशविधं प्रमेयम् । प्रवृत्तिर्धर्माधर्मो । रागद्वेषमोहा दोषाः । राग इच्छा । द्वेषो<br>मन्युः । मोहः शरीरादौ आत्मभ्रमः । प्रेत्यभावो मरणम् । फलं भोगः । अपवर्गो<br>मोक्षः । स च स्वसमानाधिकरणदुःखप्रागभावासमानकालीनदुःखध्वंसः । प्रयोजनं सुखप्राप्तिः<br>दुःखहानिश्च । दृष्टान्तो महानसादिः । प्रामाणिकत्वेन अभ्युपगतोऽर्थः सिद्धान्तः । निर्णयो<br>निश्चयः । स च प्रमाणफलम् । तत्त्वबुभुत्सोः कथा वादः । उभयसाधनवती विजिगीषुकथा<br>जल्पः । स्वपक्षस्थापनाहीना अपरपक्षविदळनमात्रावसाना वितण्डा । कथा नाम<br>नानावत्कपूर्वोत्तरपक्षप्रतिपादकवाक्यसंदर्भः । अभिप्रायान्तरेण प्रयुक्तस्यार्थान्तरं परिकल्प्य<br>दूषणं छलम् । असदुत्तरं जातिः । साधम्र्यवैधर्मोत्कर्षापकर्षवर्ण्यवर्ण्यविकल्प-<br>साध्यप्राप्यप्राप्तिप्रसंगप्रतिदृष्टान्तानुत्पत्तिसशयप्रकरणाहेत्वर्थापत्त्य विशीनोपपत्त्युपलब्ध्यनु-<br>पलब्धिनित्या नित्यकार्याकार्यसमा जातयः । वादिनोऽपजयहेतुर्निग्रहस्थानम् । तच्च<br>प्रतिज्ञाहानिः, प्रतिज्ञान्तरं, प्रतिज्ञाविरोधः, प्रतिज्ञासंन्यासः, हेत्वन्तरं, अर्थान्तरं, निरर्थकं,<br>अविज्ञातार्थकं, अपार्थकं, अप्राप्तकालं, न्यूनं, अधिकं, पुनरुक्तं, अननुभाषणं, अज्ञानं,<br>अप्रतिभा, विक्षेपः, मतानुज्ञा, पर्यनुयोज्योपेक्षणं, निरनुयोज्यानुयोगः, अपसिद्धान्तः,<br>हेत्वाभासाश्च । शेषं सुगमम् ।
            - **Item 3**:
              - **author**: English Translation
              - **commentary**: Dīpikā:<br>Now, the objection as to how the categories can be<br>enumerated as only seven when the Nyaya Sutras of Gautama<br>enumerate them as sixteen (as is evidenced by the first aphorism),<br>viz "Supreme felicity is attained by the knowledge about<br>the true nature of proof, object of knowledge, doubt, motive,<br>example, conclusion, premise, hypothetical reasoning,<br>ascertainment, disquisition, controversy, cavil, fallacy, quibbling,<br>self-contradiction, and refutation?" is replied by the Text:<br>Sarveṣām.... The meaning is that all these categories are included<br>severally in the seven categories (enumerated at the beginning<br>of this Text). <br>[127. Pramāṇa - prameya - samśaya - prayojana - drstānta - siddhānta<br>- avayava - tarka - nirnaya - vāda - jalpa - vitanda - hetvābhāsa<br>- chala - jāti - nigrahasthāna - tattwajñānāt - nihśreyas - adhigamana]<br>Objects of right knowledge are twelve (as is evidenced<br>in the Nyāyasūtras). They are: soul, body, sense, objects<br>of senses, intellect, mind, activity, fault, transmigration, result,<br>pain and release. [128. Atma - Sarīra - indriya - artha - buddhi - manas - pravṛtti<br>- dosa - pretya - bhāva - phala - duḥkha - apavargah prameyam] By pravrtti (Activity) is meant Dharma<br>and adharma (righteousness and unrighteousness). Faults (dosa)<br>are attraction, repulsion, and delusion. Attraction is desire;<br>repulsion is hatred; delusion is the erroneous identification<br>of the soul with the body etc; death is the state of transmigration;<br>fruit is the enjoyment; release is liberation and it is the<br>absolute negation of pain in Jiva when there exists in the<br>same Jīva no antecedent negation of pain. Motive is pleasure<br>and the destruction of pain. Examples are hearth etc. Conclusion<br>is the meaning arrived at from an authoritative source;<br>ascertainment is arriving at a determination and that is the<br>fruit of proof. Disquisition is the argumentation by a student<br>with a desire to know truth; controversy is the dialogue between<br>two parties with due logical method with a desire to score<br>victory over each other; cavil consists in not endeavouring<br>to establish his own side of the arguments (but ends only<br>in demolishing the opponents' view-points); arguments consist<br>in making various statements by many people by way of<br>exposition of sentences made by the proponents and opponents.<br>Quibbling is finding fault by ascribing quite a different meaning<br>to a proposition put forward with a totally different intent;<br>self-contradiction is a reply which is untimely and inopportune;<br>it is of 24 kinds of identicals in respect of resemblance,<br>difference, addition, subtraction, questionable, unquestionable,<br>alternative, thing to be established, presence, absence,<br>regression, counter-example, non-production, doubt, topic,<br>non-reason, presumption, non-difference, demonstration,<br>perception, non-perception, eternal, non-eternal, and effect.<br>[129. Sadharmya-samā, Vaidharmya-samā, utkarsa-samā,<br>apakarsa-samā, varnya-samā, avarnya-samā, vikalpa-samā, sādhya-samā,<br>prāpti-samā, aprāpti-sama, prasanga-sama, prati-drstānta-samā,<br>anutpatti-samā, samśaya-samā, prakaraņa-samā, ahetu-samā,<br>arthāpatti-samā, aviśeṣa-samā, upapatti-sama, upalabdhi-samā,<br>anupalabdhi-samā, nitya-samā, anitya-samā, and kārya-samā. \|\|<br>130. Pratijñāhāni, pratijñāntara, pratijñāvirodha, pratijñā-sannyāsa,<br>hetvantara, arthāntara, nirarthaka, avijñātārthaka, apārthaka, aprāptakāla,<br>nyūna, adhika, punarukta, ananubhāṣaņa, ajñāna, apratibhā, vikșepa,<br>matānujñā, paryanuyojyāpakşepaņa, niranuyojyānuyoga, apasiddhānta, and<br>hetvābhāsa.]
        - **Item 110**:
          - **verse_number**: `110`
          - **original_text**: _._._
          - **commentaries**:
            - **Item 1**:
              - **author**: English Paraphrase
              - **commentary**: _-_-_
            - **Item 2**:
              - **author**: Sanskrit Commentary
              - **commentary**: ननु करतलानल्संयोगे सत्यपि प्रतिबन्धके सति दाहानुत्पत्तेः शक्तिः पदार्थान्तरमिति<br>चेत् न । प्रतिबन्धकाभावस्य कार्यमात्रे कारणत्वेन शक्तेरनुपयोगात् । कारणत्वस्यैव<br>शक्तिपदार्थत्वात् । ननु भस्मादिना कांस्यादौ शुद्धिदर्शनादाधेयशक्तिरङ्गीकार्येति चेत्<br>न । भस्मादिसंयोगसमानकालीनास्पृश्यस्पर्शप्रतियोगिकयावदभावसहितभस्मादि-<br>संयोगध्वंसस्य शुद्धिपदार्थत्वात् । स्वत्वमपि न पदार्थान्तरम् यथेष्टविनियोगयोग्यत्वस्य<br>स्वत्वरूपत्वात् । तदवच्छेदकं च प्रतिग्रहादिलब्धत्वमेवेति ।
            - **Item 3**:
              - **author**: English Translation
              - **commentary**: Dīpikā:<br>Refutation (nigrahasthāna) is that which causes defeat to<br>the argumentator. (It is of 22 kinds): Hurting the proposition,<br>shifting the proposition, opposing the proposition, renouncing<br>the proposition, shifting the reason, shifting the topic, the<br>meaningless, the unintelligible, the incoherent, the untimely,<br>saying too little, saying too much, repetition, silence, ignorance,<br>non-ingenuity, evasion, admission of an opinion, over-looking<br>the censurable, censuring the non-censurable, deviating from<br>a tenet, and the semblance of a reason are the various kinds<br>of refutation. Rest is easily understood.<br>Objection: A distinct category known as Śakti has to be<br>admitted; because, it is observed that in the presence of<br>an obstructing agency the power of burning in fire is not<br>produced even when the fire is in contact with one's palm<br>of the hand.<br>Reply: It is not so; everywhere the absence of the obstructing<br>agency is indispensable only in the production of the effect<br>(here, burning) and not in producing the causal efficacy (ie<br>the presence of an obstructing agency only neutralises the<br>burning and not the heat, which causes burning). Karanatvam<br>is the meaning of the word Sakti.<br>Objection: It is observed that ingredients like ash cleanse<br>metals like lead; so we have to admit the presence of a<br>dependent power in ash.<br>Reply: It is not so; because, the power of ash to cleanse<br>the metal is the same as washing of the ash off the metal.<br>Cleanliness consists in destroying the impurity by the contact<br>of ash with a thing that is impure and which is free from<br>any cause which will make it impure again. Therefore, purity<br>is not a separate category. Thus the meaning of Purity is<br>such destruction of ashes.<br>Ownership also is not an independent category; because,<br>the true nature of ownership consists in the capability of<br>a thing to be disposed of just as one pleases, ie a thing<br>can be purchased and sold to another as one pleases.
        - **Item 111**:
          - **verse_number**: `111`
          - **original_text**: _-_-_
          - **commentaries**:
            - **Item 1**:
              - **author**: English Paraphrase
              - **commentary**: _._._
            - **Item 2**:
              - **author**: Sanskrit Commentary
              - **commentary**: अथ विधिर्निरूप्यते प्रयत्नजनकचिकीर्षाजनकज्ञानविषयो विधिः । तत्प्रतिपादको<br>लिङादिर्वा । कृत्यसाध्ये प्रवृत्त्यदर्शनात् कृतिसाध्यताज्ञानं प्रवर्तकम् । न च विषभक्षणादौ<br>प्रवृत्तिप्रसङ्गः, इष्टसाधनतालिङ्गककृतिसाध्यताज्ञानस्य काम्यस्थले विहितकालशुचि-<br>जीवित्वनिमित्तज्ञानजन्यस्य नित्यनैमित्तिकस्थले प्रवर्तकत्वात् । न चाननुगमः<br>स्वविशेषणवत्ताप्रतिसंधानजन्यत्वस्यानुगतत्वादिति गुरवः । तत् न । लाघवेन<br>कृतिसाध्येष्टसाधनताज्ञानस्यैव चिकीर्षाद्वारा प्रयत्नजनकत्वात् । न च नित्यनैमित्तिकस्थले<br>इष्टसाधनत्वाभावादप्रवृत्तिप्रसङ्गः, तत्रापि प्रत्यवायपरिहारस्य पापक्षयस्य च फलत्वकल्पनात् ।<br>तस्मात्कृतिसाध्येष्टसाधनत्वमेव लिङाद्यर्थः । ननु 'ज्योतिष्टोमेन स्वर्गकामो यजेत' इत्यत्र<br>लिङा स्वर्गसाधनमपूर्व कार्य प्रतीयते । यागस्याशुतरविनाशिनः<br>कालान्तरभाविस्वर्गसाधनत्वायोगात् तद्योग्यं स्थायिकार्यमपूर्वमेव लिङाद्यर्थः । कार्य<br>कृतिसाध्यम् । कृतेः सविषयत्वाद्विषयाकाङ्क्षायां यागो विषयत्वेनान्वेति । 'कस्य कार्यम्'<br>इति नियोज्याकाङ्क्षायां स्वर्गकामपदं नियोज्यपरतयान्वेति । कार्यबोद्धा नियोज्यः ।<br>तेन 'ज्योतिष्टोमनामकयागविषयकं स्वर्गकामस्य कार्यम्' इति वाक्यार्थः संपद्यते ।<br>वैदिकलिङ्क्त्वात् 'यावज्जीवमग्निहोत्रं जुहुयात्' इति नित्यवाक्येऽप्यपूर्वमेव वाच्यं कल्प्यते ।<br>'आरोग्यकामो भेषजपानं कुर्यात्' इत्यादिलौकिकलिङः क्रियाकार्ये लक्षणा इति चेत्<br>न । यागस्याप्ययोग्यतानिश्वयाभावेन इष्टसाधनतया प्रतीत्यनन्तरं तन्निर्वाहार्थम्<br>अवान्तख्यापारतयाऽपूर्वकल्पनात् । कीर्तनादिना नाशश्रुतेर्न यागध्वंसो व्यापारः ।<br>लोकव्युत्पत्तिबलात्क्रियायामेव कृतिसाध्येष्टसाधनत्वं लिङा बोध्यत इति लिड्त्वेन<br>विध्यर्थकत्वम्, आख्यातत्वेन यत्नार्थकत्वम् । पचति पाकं करोतीति विवरणदर्शनात्,<br>किं करोतीति प्रश्ने पचतीत्युत्तराच्चाख्यातस्य प्रयत्नार्थकत्वात् । रथो गच्छतीत्यादौ<br>अनुकूलव्यापारे लक्षणा । देवदत्तः पचति, देवदत्तेन पच्यते तण्डुलः, इत्यादौ<br>कर्तृकर्मणोर्नाख्यातार्थत्वम् । किं तु तद्गतैकत्वादीनामेव । तयोराक्षेपादेव लाभः ।<br>प्रजयतीत्यादौ धातोरेव प्रकर्षे शक्तिः । उपसर्गाणां द्योतकत्वमेव न तत्र शक्तिः ।
            - **Item 3**:
              - **author**: English Translation
              - **commentary**: Now, the meaning of injunction (vidhi) is being elucidated. An injunction is a sentence which conveys knowledge that<br>prompts a desire for action which in its turn produces an<br>effort. To prompt man to an action three conditions are<br>necessary; (a) kṛtisādhyatājñāna, the knowledge of the capability<br>to perform a task; (b) istasādhanatājñāna, the knowledge of<br>getting the desired fruit of the action, (c) balavada-<br>nistānanubandhitvajñāna, the knowledge that the performance<br>of an action is harmless. Wherever there is the knowledge<br>of incapability to accomplish a deed, there is also the absence<br>of motivation for that action. So, there must be the knowledge<br>of the possibility of accomplishing the deed. Secondly, one<br>does not undertake a deed even if one is capable of doing<br>that, if the result is harmful, eg the injunction to drink poison.<br>So there must be the knowledge of getting the desired fruit<br>of action to prompt one to activity.<br>In place of performance of rites with a desire for fruits<br>(kāmyakarma) one needs the knowledge that it is possible<br>to perform the rites accompanied by a knowledge of getting<br>the desired fruit of the rite. In places of regular and occasional<br>rites, the knowledge of (a) prescribed time, (b) one's own<br>existence; and (c) of the state of purity are the factors that<br>produce the knowledge that one ought to perform the regular<br>and occational rites.<br>Objection: Here, various reasons have been adduced for<br>the knowledge to make it capable of motivating a man to<br>activity. Why not give a general reason for the knowledge<br>that will motivate a man to activity in places of regular,<br>occasional and selfish rites? A man who is prompted to perform<br>a rite has also the knowledge of conditions pertaining to<br>those relevant rites. The knowledge of conditions pertaining<br>to each rite is the general motivation to prompt a man to<br>activity. This is the opinion of the followers of Prabhākara.<br>Reply: Now, this explanation is very elaborate. To be brief<br>we say, the motivation to perform a rite is generated from<br>a desire to perform that rite owing to the knowledge of<br>one's capacity to perform that rite accompanied by a knowledge<br>of getting the desired fruit of that rite.<br>Objection: But in places of regular and occasional rites,<br>no fruit accrues to the performer (as those rites are duty-bound).<br>So, where is the motivation in place of performance of regular<br>and occasional rites?<br>Reply: Here also there is the achievement of fruit of action<br>in the form of avoiding pratyavāya (sin occurring due to the<br>non-performance of regular and occasional rites as enjoined<br>in the scriptures) and also destroying sin. Therefore, injunction<br>is the knowledge of the capability to accomplish a rite signified<br>by words suffixed with personal endings of liṅ, lot etc.<br>The followers of Prabhākara are of the opinion that the<br>meaning of personal ending liṅ, is in apūrva (the śakti or<br>force born of a rite). In the Vedic injunction: one desiring<br>heaven ought to perform the jyotiṣṭoma sacrifice, which is suffixed<br>with personal ending liṅ, the meaning of the injunction is<br>in the rites related to jyotiṣṭoma sacrifice, the performance<br>of which produces a power called apūrva. The rite called<br>jyotiṣṭoma perishes immediately after its completion and does<br>not last till one gets the fruit (which is unseen) of that<br>rite consisting in going to heaven. We have to admit that<br>the meaning of an injunction is in the power that is produced<br>by the performance of the sacrifice and which lasts till one<br>gets the fruit. This is also known as niyoga as this apūrva<br>engages one, who is desirous of going to heaven, to perform<br>the jyotistoma sacrifice. Thus, the meaning of the injunction:<br>One desirous of attaining heaven shall perform jyotistoma sacrifice<br>is: if one entertains a desire to go to heaven, he ought<br>to strive to posses apūrva produced by the performance of<br>the jyotistoma sacrifice. Similarly, in Vedic injunction: One<br>ought to perfom agnihotra so long as one lives, the meaning<br>is indicated in the necessity to have apūrva by the performance<br>of agnihotra. But in secular injunctions like: One who desires<br>health must drink medicine, the implied meaning is in the<br>action of drinking itself.<br>Naiyāyikas: It is not so. In the absence of the knowledge<br>that the performance of jyotistoma sacrifice is not capable<br>of conferring heaven as the fruit, one possesses the knowledge<br>that the jyotistoma sacrifice is the means to get heaven. One<br>who knows this also knows that, though the fruit of getting<br>heaven is not achieved immediately by performing the sacrifice,<br>it is attained by the intermediary cause (vyāpāra) called apūrva,<br>which is produced by the performance of the jyotistoma<br>sacrifice. [131. Take for instance the sentence, "Agriculture produces food."<br>Agriculture consists in activities like tilling the land, sowing the seed<br>etc. Here, the result is not born immediately after these activities,<br>but through such intermediary causes like the crop and paddy stock.<br>Similarly, in sacrifice too, one comes to the conclusion that the<br>fruit of heaven is attained not immediately, but later through the<br>intermediary cause called apūrva which is born of the performance<br>of the sacrifice]Thus, apūrva is only a form of vyāpāra and not the<br>meaning of personal ending ling.
        - **Item 112**:
          - **verse_number**: `112`
          - **original_text**: _-_-_
          - **commentaries**:
            - **Item 1**:
              - **author**: English Paraphrase
              - **commentary**: _._._
            - **Item 2**:
              - **author**: Sanskrit Commentary
              - **commentary**: पदार्थतत्त्वज्ञानस्य परमप्रयोजनं मोक्षः । तथाहि 'आत्मा वाऽरे द्रष्टव्यः श्रोतव्यो<br>मन्तव्यो निदिध्यासितव्यः' इति श्रुत्या श्रवणादीनां आत्मसाक्षात्कारहेतुत्वबोधनात् श्रुत्वा<br>देहादिविलक्षणात्मज्ञाने सत्यप्यसंभावनानिवृत्तेर्वाक्यार्थानुसंधानरूपमननसाध्यत्वात् ।<br>मननोपयोगिपदार्थनिरूपणद्वारा शास्त्रस्यापि मोक्षोपयोगित्वम् । तदनन्तरं<br>श्रुत्युपदिष्टयोगविधिना निदिध्यासने कृते तदनन्तरं देहादिविलक्षणात्म साक्षात्कारे सति<br>देहादावहमित्यभिमानरूपमिथ्याज्ञाननाशे दोषाभावात् प्रवृत्त्यभावे धर्माधर्मयोरभावे जन्माभावे<br>पूर्वधर्माधर्मयोरनुभवेन नाशे चरमदुःखध्वंसलक्षणमोक्षो जायते । ज्ञानमेव मोक्षसाधनम् ।<br>मिथ्याज्ञाननिवृत्तेर्ज्ञानमात्रसाध्यत्वात् । 'तमेवं विदित्वाऽतिमृत्युमेति नान्यः पन्था<br>विद्यतेऽयनाय' इति श्रुत्या साधनान्तरनिषेधाच्च । ननु 'तत्प्राप्तिहेतुर्विज्ञानं कर्म चोक्तं<br>महामुने' इति कर्मणो मोक्षसाधनत्वस्मरणाज्ज्ञानकर्मणोः समुच्चय इति चेत् न ।<br>"नित्यनैमित्तिकैरेव कुर्वाणो दुरितक्षयम् । ज्ञानं च विमलीकुर्वन्नभ्यासेन च पाचयेत् ।<br>अभ्यासाच्च कचिज्ज्ञानात्कैवल्यं लभते नरः ।" इत्यादिना कर्मणो<br>ज्ञानसाधनत्वप्रतिपादनाज्ज्ञानद्वारैव कर्मणो मोक्षसाधनत्वं न साक्षात् ।<br>तस्मात्पदार्थतत्त्वज्ञानस्य मोक्षः परमप्रयोजनमिति सर्वं रमणीयम् ॥<br>इति श्रीमदन्नम्भट्टोपाध्यायविरचिता तर्कसंग्रहदीपिका समाप्ता ।।
            - **Item 3**:
              - **author**: English Translation
              - **commentary**: Dīpikā:<br>Some are of the opinion that it is only the destruction<br>of sacrifice (yāgadhvamsa) that confers the fruit of heaven.<br>Therefore, the destruction of sacrifice is the intermediary cause<br>(vyāpāra) here. Naiyāyikas do not accept this argument because<br>of the saying, virtue is destroyed if one eulogises it (kīrtanādinā<br>dharmanāśah). If you say that yāgadhvamsa (destruction of<br>sacrifice) is the virtue that will take one to heaven, we say,<br>it cannot be so; because, there can be no destruction (dhvamsa)<br>of destruction. So, we have to admit that apūrva is only<br>a vyāpāra.<br>Thus, by observing conventional behaviour, we have to<br>admit the force of the meaning of the personal ending ling<br>in the knowledge of the possibility of performing a rite along<br>with the knowledge of getting the desired fruit of that rite.<br>In the personal ending ling, there is its attribute lingatva<br>and also ākhyātatva. (All the ten la-kāras are known as ākhyāta).<br>The meaning of ākhyāta is in the effort (prayatna) involved<br>in the performance of an action, eg the action of cooking.<br>When one asks, What is he doing? one replies: he is<br>cooking, where the effort of cooking is involved. Thus by<br>ākhyāta, the meaning of effect is determined. But in places<br>where one says: The chariot is moving, we cannot say of<br>an effort on the part of the chariot which is not favourable<br>to produce the activity of moving inasmuch as effort is an<br>attribute of a sentient being. Therefore, we have to admit<br>here that ākhyāta has its implied meaning in vyāpāra.<br>The grammarians say that the meaning of ākhyāta is<br>found either in the agent (kartā) or in the action (karma).<br>This also is incorrect. In the examples: Devadatta cooks rice<br>and rice is cooked by Devadatta, the meaning of both the<br>agent and karma is got by akṣepa ie expectation of the<br>significance in them). Therefore, we have to admit the meaning<br>of ākhyāta as applying to numbers involved in the agent<br>and the action, and we get this meaning by means of akşepa.<br>In places of usage of words like, prayajati he performs<br>sacrifice excellently, the attribute of excellence does not indicate<br>the particle pra but only qualifies the verbal root yaj; because,<br>the power of a particle is only in indication and not in<br>qualifying statements.<br>Conclusion:<br>The highest aim of the knowledge of categories is liberation.<br>It is said in the Sruti: “O Maitreyi, This Ātman ought to<br>be realized, heard, reflected on and meditated upon”[132. Atma vā are drastavyaḥ, śrotavyah, mantavyah, nididhyāsitavyah ] This<br>passage proclaims the method of hearing etc as the means<br>for having an immediate and direct knowledge of Atman.<br>Though one hears the Vedic passages proclaiming that the<br>Soul is quite distinct from the body etc one does not get<br>rid of disbelief (asambhāvanā) etc. This disbelief etc are removed<br>by constant reflection on the Vedic teachings with the help<br>of reasoning. Reasoning is impossible in the absence of a<br>knowledge of the categories. Therefore, a knowledge of the<br>categories is the means (though not the direct means) that<br>produces the knowledge of the Soul. After this, one ought<br>to constantly reflect and meditate on the true nature of the<br>Soul following the instructions of the Sruti. Then one gets<br>the direct knowledge of the Soul as quite distinct from body<br>etc. From this occurs the destruction of false knowledge that<br>causes erroneous identification of the soul with body etc by<br>producing the notion: I am this body. With the elimination<br>of erroneous knowledge, its attendant evils are also eliminated.<br>With the elimination of evil, there occurs the absence of<br>effort (as no desire is left in the mind with the destruction<br>of ignorance). In the absence of effort, there is the absence<br>of both merit and demerit. With its elimination, the cycle<br>of transmigration in the form of birth etc also gets eliminated.<br>With the destruction of rebirth, the stored results of past<br>deeds, virtuous and non-virtuous, get exhausted by experiencing<br>them; with the exhaustion of all the results of past action,<br>one attains liberation characterised by the absolute destruction<br>of pain. Therefore, knowledge alone is the means of attaining<br>liberation since it is caused by knowledge alone on the destruction<br>of erroneous knowledge. The Sruti passage: "One attains the<br>state of immortality by knowing Him alone; here there is<br>no other way," prohibits means other than knowledge of<br>the Soul to attain liberation.[133. Tameva viditvātimṛtyumti nānyah panthā vidyate'yanāya ]<br>Objection: There is a doubt here; it is said: "O great Muni,<br>it is said that karma and jñāna are the causes of attaining<br>liberation. [134. Tat prāptiheturvijñānam karma coktam mahāmune ]Here, action also is prescribed as a means to<br>attaining liberation. So, let it be said, that both action and<br>knowledge conjointly produce liberation.<br>Reply: It is not so; by passages like: "It is only the<br>performance of nitya and naimittika rites that leads to the<br>destruction of effects of evil actions; knowledge purifies the<br>mind and attains maturity by constant practice; from constant<br>practice man attains liberation characterised by ripe<br>knowledge", [135. Nityanaimittkaireva kurvāņo duritakşayam, jñānam ca vimali-<br>kurvannabhyāsena ca pācayet; Abhyāsāt ca kvacitjñānāt, Kaivalyam labhate<br>narah ]it is taught that karma only leads to knowledge.<br>Thus karma becomes the means for liberation only through<br>knowledge, and not directly. Thus, the highest aim of the<br>knowledge of the categories is liberation. So, this Text is<br>worthy of respectful study by all who aim at liberation.
        - **Item 113**:

            - **Item 2**:
              - **author**: Sanskrit Commentary
              - **commentary**: कणादन्यायमतयोर्बालव्युत्पत्तिसिद्धये । अन्नंभट्टेन विदुषा रचित-<br>स्तर्कसंग्रहः ॥ इति श्रीमहामहोपाध्याय अन्नंभट्टविरचित-<br>तर्कसंग्रहः समाप्तः ॥
            - **Item 3**:
              - **author**: English Translation
              - **commentary**: The wise Annambhatta composed this Tarkasamgraha with<br>a view to making the systems of Gautama and Kanāda easily<br>comprehensible to beginners.<br>Here ends the Tarka-samgraha of Annambhatta along with<br>his Dīpikā.
